The Ministry of Communications Revises the Contents of the Mackay Contract 75

Regarding the Contract Signed by Chen Mingshu

Clauses Unfavorable to Us Are Completely Deleted

The Aircraft Purchase Contract Is Canceled and Renegotiated

The Mackay Communications Contract and the China Electric Company Aircraft Purchase Contract were formally signed in July of last year by Minister of Communications Chen Mingshu with the American Mackay Company and the China Electric Company. Subsequently, the contents and clauses of the Mackay Communications Contract were found to have points unfavorable to us. Furthermore, the China Electric Company Aircraft Purchase Contract, regarding the purchase of equipment including a wireless telephone super-power radio station and four small radio stations, considering the current situation in our country, international wireless telephone communication is not yet very urgent. The price reached a huge sum of US$310,000, which seems difficult to raise. The repayment method was also taken from the telephone and telegraph income of the Mackay Communications Contract. The engineering management was also authorized to the China Electric Company. All of this exceeded the scope of a normal sales contract. Therefore, after the two contracts were formally signed, there was national public opposition, and the Ministry of Communications once again discussed canceling them. However, because it involved canceling signed contracts, repeated negotiations with the companies were unsuccessful, and they insisted on not agreeing. Only in October of last year was the China Electric Company willing to reduce the price of the aircraft to US$250,000 as a concession. The Ministry of Communications considered that the remaining conditions were still harsh and did not immediately agree. When Zhu Jia骅 succeeded Chen Mingshu as Minister of Communications, he continued to actively negotiate. However, because the contracts had already been formally signed and the companies insisted on not conceding, for the sake of government credibility and factual difficulties, completely canceling the contracts proved to be difficult due to reason and reality. Therefore, the negotiations had to change direction. For the Mackay contract, the points unfavorable to us were deleted and revised. For the China Electric Company aircraft purchase contract, it was completely canceled and reorganized. The purchase list was further reduced in price, and a new aircraft purchase contract based on a purely commercial sales agreement was drawn up. The right to manage the project was recovered, and it was ensured that it was not related to the Mackay Communications Contract. Furthermore, funds were allocated from the Sino-British Boxer Indemnity Funds for the Huai River Commission's London material procurement, to be procured by the London China Purchasing Committee, so as not to be subjected to any constraints. The Ministry of Communications submitted the details of the negotiation process and revision methods to the Executive Yuan meeting this Wednesday, which was approved and formally signed yesterday (the 7th). The main points of the two contracts are recorded as follows:

Key Points of the Revised Mackay Contract 76

(1) Direct communication is limited to the United States. The original contract stipulated that direct communication locations included Hawaii and the Philippines in addition to the United States. Because our international radio station's current receiving equipment is not sufficient and there is not much telegraph communication between the two locations, one circuit is sufficient. The revised direct destination is only the United States, but it is stipulated that if the Sino-US direct circuit is blocked, it can be relayed through the Philippine radio station, but the sharing of fees is still the same as direct telegraphs. (2) Equal sharing of circuit fees. The original contract stipulated that the radio circuit fee was two-thirds for the transmitting side and one-third for the receiving side. However, our outbound telegraphs are limited to those with route identification, while all of Mackay's telegraphs, except for those with other designated routes, must be forwarded through this route. The number of inbound telegraphs will inevitably be greater than the number of outbound telegraphs, and their fees will be higher than ours. This modification is for both parties to share equally, which is more beneficial to us. (3) Cancellation of the provision to distribute outbound telegraph paper printed with route identification. Article 11 of the original contract contained the above provision. The Ministry of Communications considered that our communications contracts with various foreign companies did not have such a precedent. This modification has been canceled. (4) Deletion of words involving South American international communications. The original contract contained clauses involving international communications with South American countries. The Ministry of Communications believes that when our country's international communications industry develops in the future, international communications may be monopolized by the Mackay Company, and there is a risk of future misinterpretation of the contract, leading to disputes. This modification has been deleted. (5) The contract is mainly in Chinese.

Key Points of the Separately Agreed Upon Aircraft Purchase Agency 77

(1) Purely a sales contract. The original contract and the conditions of the revised contract stipulated that when the Ministry signs telephone contracts with other countries, the company agrees to assist, use the telegraph and telephone revenue from the Mackay Communications Contract to pay off the unpaid equipment price, and have the company recommend an engineering manager, etc., which exceeded the scope of a sales contract and were actually unfavorable to us. This time, when the Ministry of Communications discussed purchasing aircraft with the company, it ignored the original contract and determined that the purchase of equipment was purely a commercial sales contract and should not involve personnel administration and other issues, so as to avoid extraneous matters. This new contract was based on this principle. As for the funds for purchasing equipment, the Ministry of Communications, under very difficult economic circumstances, plans to allocate funds from the British Boxer Indemnity for the Huai River Commission's London material procurement, to be procured by the London China Purchasing Committee, to transact with the company in cash and never incur debts, so as to avoid being constrained. (2) Selection of equipment. The original contract stipulated the purchase of one super-power radio station and four small radio stations. In the current situation in our country, international telephone communication cannot be very developed at the beginning, and Marconi radio stations also have broadcasting telephone equipment. It is only necessary to add a receiving station and a telephone connection machine and a secret telephone machine. Therefore, it was decided not to purchase a super-power radio station. However, small telephone stations are needed because our country's important long-distance telephone lines, such as Beijing-Tianjin, Pinghan (Beijing-Hankou), Shanghai-Hankou, are all lacking. Therefore, it is planned to expand these by purchasing three for application. The rest will be used to carefully select the equipment that our country urgently needs, reduce prices, and increase purchases. The important equipment to be purchased this time includes: (1) three small wireless telegraph and telephone dual-use transmitting stations; (2) three automatic telegraph machines; (3) six Type II receiving stations; (4) four telephone connection machines; (5) four secret telephone machines; (6) two Type III receiving stations; together with antennas, vacuum tubes, and engines, etc., totaling 48,000 British pounds. The Ministry of Communications inquired about this price from various countries and compared it with other telegraph stations and broadcasting telephone stations, and it was extremely fair.

Page 10

The Discovery of Antiquities in Teng County 78

Teng County Dispatch: Teng County in southern Shandong, formerly the State of Teng in the Zhou Dynasty, has a history of more than 2,000 years. The tomb of Duke Wen of Teng is located in the county seat, which was the Temple of Literature during the Qing Dynasty and is now Zhongshan Square. Although the [foundation] has disappeared, the people of the county still mention it. Recently, fourteen antiquities, including ding (tripod), pan (dish), and yi (ewer), were discovered in Anshang Village, Eighth Township, Second District of Teng County, attracting great attention in society. Han Fuju, Chairman of the Shandong Provincial Government, and He Siyuan, Director of the Department of Education, believe that Teng County has such a long history in our country's past, and now the discovery of these antiquities is undoubtedly excellent material for scholars studying and writing national history. They immediately sent telegrams to the Teng County Government to properly preserve them, and also dispatched Wang Xiantang, Director of the Shandong Provincial Library, to personally investigate in Teng County. Wang (Xiantang) left Jinan on April 4th. Since the news of the discovery of antiquities in various places has been emerging in recent years, reporters often regret not being able to personally witness them and provide readers with accurate reports. Now that the authorities attach such importance to antiquities, and Wang Xiantang, who is knowledgeable about antiquities, is sent to Teng County for investigation, it is expected that this trip will have some contributions. Moreover, Teng County is only 500 li from Jinan, and the Pingpu train can reach it in eight hours. Therefore, the reporter took the Ping 201 train south from Jinan at 9:40 a.m. the next day (the 5th) of Wang's departure, arriving in Teng County at 5 p.m. that afternoon, and immediately went to the county government to inquire about everything. County Magistrate Cui Gongfu and local representatives were holding a variety show (drama) at Zhongshan Square to raise funds to comfort the soldiers at the front. Therefore, his secretary, Shen Liangjie, received the reporter on his behalf.

Shen Liangjie's Statement 79

According to his statement, the antiquities were discovered by Chen Shifa, a farmer in Anshang Village, Eighth Township, Second District of the county, who also runs a tofu business. In the spring, Chen Shifa was plowing his land and plowed out a broken pot. After uncovering the pot, he saw a hole, so he continued to dig down and found two ancient tripods, one ancient dish, and four ancient ewers, all with lids, and arranged neatly, without any damage. At that time, Chen (Shifa) did not know what they were, so he picked them all up and took them home. Later, they were all sold at low prices. After Chen told people about the shape of the items he picked up that day, they determined that the items were ancient tripods, dishes, and ewers. Chen could not name them, let alone know that they were invaluable treasures related to history and culture. After the county government learned about it, it dispatched Wei Xihong and Bian Qiushui, section chiefs of the Fifth Section (formerly the County Education Bureau), to investigate in the countryside. It was confirmed that the antiquities had been sold and were no longer in Chen's possession. According to Section Chief Wei (Xihong), there were fourteen pieces of ancient objects. Chen Zhonghai, the township chief of the Eighth Township, reported to the county government that there were four pieces. After Chairman (Han Fuju) learned about it, he ordered the county to cooperate with Wang Xiantang, the director of the Provincial Library, Zhang Shushen, a candidate official from the Provincial Government, and Liu Xianting, the director of the Provincial Public Security Bureau, who were sent by the Provincial Government, and bring the township chief to handle the matter. According to the order, Chen Zhonghai reported that there were eleven pieces. In short, the exact number of ancient objects is currently being investigated, and there is no talk of how to preserve them in the future. Director Wang (Xiantang), Director Liu (Xianting), and candidate official Zhang (Shushen) are currently staying at Fuxinggong General Merchandise Store in the city. It is said that they have gone to the countryside today. The reporter then copied the original text of Chairman Han's instruction and left.

Han Fuju's Instruction 80

To issue an order: It is recently reported by Chen Zhonghai, the township chief of the Eighth Township in the county, that a farmer named Chen in Anshang Village in the district has obtained eleven pieces of antiquities and requests that officials be sent to escort them all to the province for disposal. In addition to the separate order, Zhang Shushen, a candidate official from the Provincial Government, Liu Xianting, the director of the Provincial Public Security Bureau, and Wang Xiantang, the director of the Provincial Library, are specially dispatched to bring the township chief Chen Zhonghai to cooperate with the county magistrate in handling the matter. The county magistrate should immediately comply with the order and report the situation for review. This order.

At this time, it was already 9 p.m., and the weather was cloudy with occasional rain. The reporter originally intended to continue the investigation, but it was too late, and it was the first time in this place, unfamiliar with both people and the area. Therefore, the reporter decided to work tomorrow and decided to first visit the committee members sent by the province to find out the whereabouts of the antiquities and then visit them. Despite the rain, the reporter set out, although the streets were repaired with roads (the section from the station to the west city gate), they were too narrow and pedestrians trampled them back and forth, resulting in a mixture of mud and water, which could reach the ankles. The reporter could not help but secretly say, "This is truly (impossible to walk, brother)". After entering the city, the road was paved with stones, which was not very wide either. At eight o'clock, the reporter arrived at Fuxinggong General Merchandise Store. The store clerk told the reporter that the Wang committee members had just gone to the county government and might not have arrived yet. The reporter then rushed to the county government and submitted a card to request an audience with County Magistrate Cui and Director Wang, etc. (the county people generally call Wang, etc. as committee members). County Magistrate Cui (Gongfu) received the reporter and introduced the reporter to Wang, etc. After a few words of greeting, County Magistrate (Gongfu) led the way to see the antiquities. The antiquities were transported from the township and stored in the outer room of the county magistrate's office. At that time, there were many local gentry and students watching. Upon closer inspection, there were eleven pieces of tripods, yi, qiao (percussion instrument), [missing text], etc., all covered with green rust. When tapped, they made a clear sound, and they were indeed not modern objects. At that time, Chen Zhonghai, the township chief of the Eighth Township, was also present and asked about the location where the antiquities were discovered. The township chief hesitated and could not speak, so Liu Xianting, the director of the Jinan Municipal Women's Vocational Training Institute, spoke on his behalf. It was then learned that the antiquities were discovered

The Location Where Antiquities Appeared 81

Is located about a li north of Anshang Village, commonly known as Tutuding, bordering Taoshan to the west and Shaji River to the east, covering an area of about three mu. The terrain is elevated like a mound. The surrounding area is yellow soil, but the middle is gray. According to general speculation, it is an ancient tomb for many years. I don't know how many vicissitudes have caused such a change. The landlord here belongs to the Chen family, cultivated by Chen Shifa and Chen Shifu brothers for generations. On the seventeenth day of the lunar calendar of this year, because there was a ditch in the land, they went to level it in order to plant. Accidentally, they dug out a pot-shaped metal fragment. After digging down more than two feet, they found antiquities. Chen transported them to his home. Later, the villagers all knew about it, and some even went to dig secretly at night. Now, thanks to the official's efforts to preserve them, the following numbers have been obtained.

Number of Antiquities 82

Including one tripod, one dish, one yi, [missing text], and ge (cooking pot), four each. There are also six kinds of parts, all attached to ancient objects, totaling seventeen pieces in size. One of the four [missing text] has words on the bottom, which are in seal script, but they are blurred and almost unrecognizable. With the best of eyesight, only one "Meng" character and the four characters "zi sun yong yong" (may descendants use forever) in the last line can be vaguely identified. As for whether there are any words on other antiquities, it is currently unknown because of the soil rust covering them. According to the director of the Provincial Library

Wang Xiantang's Appraisal 83

Wang Xiantang determined that these antiquities were from the Zhou Dynasty. Wang also said that when the antiquities were first discovered, there were fish bones and animal teeth (like cow teeth) in the tripod, and there were also fragments of tiles and mussel shells beside it. Because the villagers were ignorant, they have all been discarded. If these items existed, they could be identified as from the Western Zhou Dynasty, because shells were used as currency during the Zhou Dynasty. As for

The Disposal of Antiquities 84

Regarding the disposal of antiquities, the committee members Zhang Shushen, Liu Xianting, Wang Xiantang, and County Magistrate Cui Gongfu, who were sent by the provincial government, decided at that time to first take a photo to keep as a souvenir, and then pack them in boxes and transport them to Jinan, and then determine the location for preservation. At the same time, the committee members and County Magistrate Cui will jointly draft a memorial to report to Chairman Han. At that time, Section Chief Wei (Xihong) had a temporary exhibition so that the people of the county could have a considerable understanding of the antiquities. Because they were in a hurry to nail the boxes and transport them to the province, it could not be realized. So, they took a photo in the second hall of the county government and divided them into two wooden boxes (used to hold matches). Wang Xiantang personally placed them, and County Magistrate Cui Gongfu and Fifth Section Chief Wei Xihong, etc., were all on-site to supervise. After the installation was completed, three seals were vertically and horizontally pasted on the bottom cover of each wooden box, and they will be shipped to Jinan tomorrow (the 7th).

Wei Xihong's Statement 85

Wei Xihong, the chief of the Fifth Section, said that at the end of last month, he received a report from a villager saying that farmers named Chen in Anshang Village had discovered many kinds of antiquities, and antique dealers from Jinan were willing to pay 2,000 yuan to buy them, and they were currently discussing the price. He believed that since antique dealers had come from afar and were willing to pay a high price to buy these antiquities, they must have their value and history. Moreover, the current Teng County is the ancient State of Teng, and it is adjacent to the birthplace of the two great sages of our country, Confucius and Mencius (Qufu and Zou County), and its relationship in history and culture is very important and great. He decided not to let them be lost. So, on the one hand, in the name of an education inspector, he telegraphed to Director He Siyuan, and on the other hand, in the name of the chief of the Fifth Section, he signed a report to the county magistrate of this county (Cui Gongfu). Soon, Director He replied to the county by telegram, ordering him to properly preserve them to prevent them from being lost. At the same time, Li Shuchun, Director of the Department of Civil Affairs, also sent a telegram to the county. County Magistrate Cui of this county then sent him and Bian Qiushui, the dispatch director of the county government, Li Shichen, the county school supervisor, Xu Zhongshan, a staff member of the public education center, and Zhu Chuanzhe, the district chief of the Second District, to investigate. He and others went together on the first day of this month. After meeting with Chen Zhonghai, the township chief of the Second Township, and Chen Shifa and Chen Shifu, the brothers who excavated the antiquities, he explained the purpose of the visit. However, the villagers were ignorant and afraid that the government would confiscate them, so they did not offer the antiquities and said that they had already been sold. When asked for the names of the buyers, they said they did not know. The final result on that day was that Chen Zhonghai, the township chief of the Eighth Township, made a guarantee that he would collect the antiquities the next day and would not allow them to be sold. The second time the county magistrate sent people to the countryside to transport the antiquities, Chen Zhonghai, the township chief, and the Chen brothers all avoided meeting them. When Chairman Han learned about it in the province, he asked Liu Xianting, the current director of the Jinan Municipal Women's Vocational Training Institute, because Director Liu was from Teng County and was also a neighbor of the Chen family. Director Liu then sent a letter from Jinan to Chen Zhonghai, summoning him to the province to meet Chairman Han. After Chen Zhonghai arrived in the province and met Chairman Han, he was willing to send the antiquities to the province for preservation. After Chen returned to the county from the province, he did not fully deliver all seventeen antiquities, large and small, to the county government until yesterday (the 5th).

Situation of On-Site Investigation 86

Wei Xihong, the chief of the Fifth Section of Teng County, and Zhu Chuanzhe, the district chief of the Second District, signed a report to the county magistrate after the investigation, saying that it was about signing a report. In the case of discovering antiquities in Anshang Village in the east of the city, in accordance with your hand instructions, they immediately went to verify on the 1st of this month. It is now found that the location where the antiquities were discovered is about a li north of the village, connecting Taoshan to the west and adjacent to the Shaji River to the east. The land is high, covering more than one mu. The surrounding area is yellow soil. The place where the antiquities were excavated is in the center of the land. The soil is loose and gray, which is obviously an ancient tomb. Due to the long years, the lime has changed. The landowners of this land are the Chen Shifu and Chen Shifa brothers, who are both old and make a living by selling tofu and bean sprouts. On the seventeenth day of the lunar calendar, because of the padding of the moat, they dug out the antiquities. When asked the township chief of the township, Chen Zhonghai, he hesitated (only) to say that he dug out two or three pieces. After asking Chen Shifa, he said that he dug out six or seven pieces, and said that he had already sold them. When asked for the name of the buyer, he said he didn't know. After many inquiries, the villagers and neighboring villagers all said that they had unearthed fourteen antiquities, including two tripods (each tripod weighs 18 and a half kilograms with thirty-four characters on the bottom), one copper plate (with words on the bottom), two copper bottles, four incense burners, one copper ladle (tiger head shape), and four copper pots. Only the tripod is green, and the rest are black. When struck, they all make a clear sound, and they are indeed ancient objects. It is said that Chen hid the antiquities in various places one day after he obtained them, and kept them secret. Moreover, he is frivolous and ignorant and has no preconceived notions. How to sell them depends on the township chief, Chen Zhonghai. He explained to the township chief, Chen Zhonghai, and the excavator the intention to investigate and persuaded them to take them out for examination. After repeated persuasion, he agreed to make a guarantee and allow the four excavated antiquities to be handed over the next day, etc. For this reason, the details of the process should be signed and reported together. (April 6th)

Xiesheng Cloth Factory Completely Destroyed by Fire 92

The Xiesheng Cloth Factory at No. 3, Liu Lane, West Heng Street, Wu County, was opened by Xu Hankang and others from Jiangyin and has been in operation for many years. It is one of the oldest cloth factories, with more than 50 factory buildings and excellent business. Unexpectedly, at around 3:00 AM on the 8th, when the workers were working, the machinery suddenly became careless, and the fire spread immediately. At this time, the wind was very strong, causing all the houses, machinery, and cloth to be completely burned. Fortunately, all the male and female workers escaped from the back door. After investigation, the loss was about 100,000 yuan. The insurance was only 30,000 yuan.

Letter from the Zhejiang Construction Bureau 95

I recently read your newspaper's report on April 8th about "Suppressing Yu Hang Native Tobacco," which stated, "After the first riot in Yu Hang, the Construction Bureau sent Zhang Fancun, a section chief, and others to investigate. The villagers, upon hearing that the provincial officials had arrived, blocked the road and knelt down, begging for a temporary suspension of the suppression, causing Zhang's car to suddenly speed away, injuring many villagers. The villagers, feeling that they were not getting what they wanted, continued to riot on the 5th and 6th," which is quite shocking. This bureau previously instructed the county magistrate of Yu Hang County to convene local gentry to a meeting to thoroughly explain the matter of suppressing native tobacco, and also sent Jiang Jiamei, a secretary of this bureau, and Zhang Fancun, a section chief, to attend the meeting. After the meeting, they returned to Hang Zhou. Although there were many farmers gathered on both sides of the bus station, there were no conflicts. Moreover, at that time, a large bus led the way, and Secretary Jiang and Section Chief Zhang were in a small car, following behind. Since the small car was closely following the large car, how could it speed up and rush forward, injuring the farmers? Your newspaper's report is based on false rumors. Furthermore, this bureau sent Secretary Jiang and others to the county for a meeting on March 30th, while the second riot occurred on April 5th, five days apart, which has nothing to do with the section chief and others. This news report is feared to be a propaganda by those who mistakenly believe in other actors. A special letter is sent to solemnly declare this, hoping that you will investigate and correct it to avoid misunderstandings. Sincerely, the Construction Bureau of the Zhejiang Provincial Government, April 8th.

Tie Zhan Gu Meng Xu 96

Preface to the Special Issue of the National Railway Line Product Exhibition by Gu Mengyu 97

The National Railway Line Product Exhibition, after nine months of preparation, has opened today. Its important significance lies in several things. The principle of national economy lies in adjusting surpluses and deficits, considering what is available and what is not, distributing them in a balanced way, and ensuring that supply and demand can meet. This is the principle of national economy and also the principle of commerce. The purpose of this exhibition is to enable the production areas and the sales areas to communicate with each other, to adjust the surplus and shortage of production in various places, to enable people to understand the products and output along the national railway lines, as well as the transportation methods, and to enable business operators to have accurate statistics and detailed budgets, so as to incorporate their operations into rationalization, and the national economy can gradually develop in a balanced way. This is the primary meaning of this exhibition. The relationship between railway undertakings and industry and commerce is mutually causal. Railways can promote the development of industry and commerce, and the railways themselves also rely on the development of industry and commerce to become more prosperous. Now, agriculture, industry, commerce, and mining are declining day by day, and the railway business is also declining day by day. For the sake of revitalizing the railway business, we must support agriculture, industry, commerce, and mining to seek the simultaneous prosperity of branches and trunks. This is another meaning of this exhibition. With our country's vast land and abundant resources, and large population, all industrial and commercial undertakings are declining to this extreme. The economic aggression of imperialism is a heavy blow, but the government's failure to fulfill its advocacy ability and responsibility is also one of the main reasons. The purpose of this exhibition is to arouse the attention and interest of the majority of people, so that the quantity of production, the scope of sales, and the calculation of transportation can have accurate statistics, as a reliable reference for operators, so that the unproductive speculative undertakings in the city can gradually turn into legitimate industrial and commercial investments. This is the third meaning of this exhibition.

The four borders are in danger, and the flames of war are raging. We are shocked by the urgency of the national crisis and believe that the basic work of enriching national power cannot be delayed. Although there are many aspects of this kind of work, the common goal should be to seek social stability and economic development, so as to increase the national production capacity. Only when internal strength is abundant can we talk about resisting foreign aggression. This is also the intention of this exhibition to actively prepare for the opening during this critical period. The storm is dark, and the rooster crows endlessly. Work hard to cultivate the fields, and look forward to it. April 10, 1933.

Developing People's Productivity by Wang Zhaoti 98

Inaugural Address by Yu Tan 99

Our country's great illness is only weakness and poverty, and poverty is the root cause of accumulated weakness. Therefore, when we talk about saving the country today, we should increase national wealth as an urgent task. And there is no other way to increase national wealth than to revitalize industry and develop the people's productivity. This is a very clear principle and does not need to be explained in detail. However, the revitalization of industry must rely on transportation, especially railway transportation. In terms of industry, it is necessary to seek a rich source of raw materials and cheap purchase prices, and a wide sales route for manufactured products and high selling prices. A rich source and a wide sales route must rely on the convenience of transportation, and cheap purchase prices and high selling prices must rely on low freight rates. In terms of commerce, it is necessary to seek a wide variety of goods for sale and large sales volume. A wide variety depends on the convenience of transportation, and large sales volume depends on low freight rates. In terms of agriculture, mining, and forestry, it is necessary to seek a wide sales route and high selling prices. A wide sales route also depends on the convenience of transportation, and high selling prices also depend on low freight rates. Therefore, it is very clear that industry relies on transportation. Modern transportation facilities include airplanes, automobiles, ships, and railways. Airplanes are only limited to transporting a small number of passengers and light mail, and automobiles are only convenient for short-distance light transportation. As for long-distance bulk goods, ships and railways are the main means of transportation. However, ships may be prevented by winter ice or wind and rain, and cannot operate accurately all year round. Their speed is also far inferior to that of railways. Moreover, the land of a country has limited navigable areas, which is not as far-reaching as railways. Therefore, there is no doubt that railways occupy the most important position in modern transportation facilities. This is why the Premier said that transportation is the mother of industry, and railways are the mother of transportation. Industry relies on railways, and railways also rely on industry. Railway business can be roughly divided into passenger transport and freight transport. In terms of business revenue, except for a very small number of lines, freight transport is actually more important than passenger transport. To develop railway business, neither of the two can be neglected. However, since railways are mainly engaged in freight transport, the quantity of freight transport can affect the prosperity of railway business. And the quantity of freight transport will naturally change with the rise and fall of agriculture, industry, mining, forestry, and other industries along the line. Moreover, when freight transport is flourishing, passenger transport will also increase accordingly. Therefore, the prosperity of railways also depends on the development of industry. The relationship between industry and railways is like that between lips and teeth, as mentioned above. Therefore, it can be seen that developing railways must promote industry, and promoting industry is developing railways. Examining the historical relationship between railways and industry in Europe and the United States, American industry was developed by the convenience of railways, while European railways were promoted by the prosperity of industry. Their mutual relationship is like this. Our country's industry and railways are both in their infancy and should be developed separately, but it is especially important to cooperate to seek common prosperity. This exhibition of railway line products organized by this ministry from the position of railways is based on this purpose. The purpose of this ministry in organizing the exhibition is to promote the development of railways and industry, and it is also believed that this exhibition is the most effective method to achieve this goal. Because our country's railways and industry are underdeveloped, the country's production cannot be used to adjust surpluses and deficits and balance supply and demand. Often, what is discarded in this place is what is urgently needed in that place. This place has a surplus of domestic products, while that place uses similar foreign goods, causing raw materials to be discarded, industry to decline, and railway business to be depressed. This exhibition gathers various kinds of goods from along the railway line in one room, clearly marking their place of origin, sales location, freight rate, etc. Visitors can distinguish the quality of the goods and understand the various related situations. Then, the surplus goods can be sold to the areas where they are needed. In the areas where there is a surplus, the prices must be low, and in the areas where there is a need, the prices must be high. This one transfer not only allows the raw materials to be used, supply and demand to be balanced, but also allows the operators to make a profit. For the sake of opening up, it directly develops agriculture, industry, commerce, mining, forestry, and other industries, and indirectly develops railway business. This association began preparations in the spring of last year. The ministry sent documents to the national railways and the governments of various provinces and cities along the line, and sent letters to various agricultural, industrial, and commercial organizations to collect products. It took half a year to complete the preparations. The collected items can be roughly divided into seven categories: agricultural products, forest products, mineral products, aquatic products, handicrafts, poultry, and medicinal materials, totaling more than 10,000 varieties. Although most of them are familiar to us, and there are no rare treasures or exquisite crafts to dazzle the audience, they are all the daily necessities of the Chinese people. This also focuses on practical people's livelihood. This association adopts the method of roving exhibition, and plans to hold meetings in various places along the national railway in turn, so as to deeply imprint this miniature of the crystallization of the national industry in the minds of people from all walks of life, so as to achieve the effect of advertising and avoid the disadvantages of being too heavy. Although the exhibition in Shanghai is temporary, it is hoped that the audience from all walks of life will be very extravagant. Because this association itself only has methods and ways to develop industry and railways, if it wants to achieve its specific realization, so as to achieve this goal, on the ministry's side, it should devote itself to the full convenience of transportation, the lowest possible freight rates, and the active construction of new roads. On the audience's side, it must also occupy its own position and make the greatest efforts in various industries, so that the division of labor and cooperation can be mutually beneficial, and industry and railways can be developed simultaneously, and the country can be transformed from poverty to wealth and from weakness to strength. This is what I sincerely welcome you to visit, and what I wish to pray for before all of you. The demand for goods is mostly time-sensitive. If it cannot be supplied in time during the time of demand, the effect of corresponding supply and demand will be lost. As a result, it will also affect the development of industry and commerce. Railway freight is an element that constitutes the market price of goods. The railway's great long-distance transportation capacity is the most effective tool for promoting the sales of goods. Its convenient and rapid transportation is a feature that meets the time-sensitive needs of goods. Therefore, railway transportation has the inherent ability to influence industry and commerce. If we can fully and properly use the inherent ability of railway transportation, then the development of industry and commerce can be expected day by day. However, for decades, our railways have not fully expressed their inherent ability, and the industrial and commercial sectors have not fully utilized the inherent ability of railways to seek the development of industry and commerce. Therefore, the phenomenon of today's industrial and commercial stagnation and backward production has formed. The National Railway Line Product Exhibition held by the Ministry of Railways this time is a strategy to solve this problem. Therefore, this exhibition is very worthy of our attention. It has special characteristics and special value. Since it is standing on the position of railways to seek industry and commerce, this is a manifestation of the railway serving the people.

Method The national people (especially the agricultural, industrial and commercial sectors)

Pay special attention to this Don't just look around and get excited

Ye Gongchuo's words

The Nature and Value of the Railway Exhibition by Tan Yaozong 100

Because of backward production in our country, people's livelihoods are deteriorating, and the national social economy is becoming increasingly difficult. It is almost that the people are poor and the wealth is exhausted, and there is a trend of national bankruptcy. The reasons for the backward production are indeed diverse, but the stagnation of industry and commerce is the biggest reason for the backward production. Because our industry and commerce are not prosperous, they are not enough to compete with other countries. Not only can the goods we produce not be sold to other countries, but also the position of the goods we produce in our own domestic market is occupied by foreign goods. Almost the entire country has become a market for foreign goods. Our own production has no foothold, and the result is naturally a trend of decline. The more our production declines, the more the power of foreign goods to invade expands. If this continues, how can we not go bankrupt? Therefore, if we want to solve the people's livelihood and develop the national social economy, we must find ways to increase our production. If we want to increase our production, we must find ways to develop our industry and commerce. Although there are many main strategies for developing our industry and commerce, the most powerful way to develop industry and commerce is railway transportation. If we can use railway transportation to regulate the production and sales and supply and demand of goods, and use railway transportation to encourage the enterprising spirit of industrialists and businessmen, our industry and commerce will naturally have considerable progress. Because railway transportation has the inherent ability to develop industry and commerce, it is closely related to industry and commerce. Whether or not industry and commerce can develop depends on whether the supply and demand of goods can correspond. Whether or not the supply and demand can correspond includes several related conditions: (1) The cost of goods The cost of goods is related to the ability to purchase. If the cost of goods is too high, the selling price must be expensive. If the selling price exceeds the general ability to purchase, the goods will not be able to be sold. As a result, supply and demand cannot correspond. If supply and demand cannot correspond, industry and commerce will have no hope of development. (2) The sales market of goods The sales market of goods is related to the production of goods. If the sales market cannot be promoted, the production must not be increased. If the production cannot be increased, it must

If the supply does not meet the demand, the result is that industry and commerce also have no hope of development (3) External view of the railway exhibition

The development of the industry, in order to promote the increase in production, then its role is naturally different from ordinary general exhibitions. Ordinary general exhibitions are mostly only in the passive aspect of observation, comparing their effects, only can make people get a sense of good and bad and impression, as to how to apply the feeling to the actual situation, in the general exhibition itself, there is no ability to promote this second step of work, so general exhibitions, can receive real effect is very few, the Ministry of Railways National Railway Line Production Goods Exhibition, on the one hand, is by means of goods exhibition to enable the audience to have a considerable understanding of the production and sales situation of various goods within the scope of the national railway transportation, so that they have a considerable standard for managing industrial and commercial industries, so that they know how to use railway transportation to make the tool of managing industrial and commercial industries, so that they know that the relationship between industrial and commercial industries and railway transportation is close, and there is a need to cooperate with railways, on the other hand, is by means of the exhibition of goods, to explore the real situation of goods production and sales, and the true situation of supply and demand, how to make the railway transportation strategy suitable for the needs of industrialists and businessmen, in order to promote the increase of production, not only in the passive aspect of observation comparison, in other words, the Ministry of Railways National Railway Line Production Goods Exhibition, is the medium of cooperation between railways and National Railway Line Production Goods Exhibition Special Issue 103

Developing the national economy by the people of the time

Railway business turns from passive to active mode by Huang Boqiao 104

The railway business is a monopoly business, but the meaning of this monopoly is only to say that under certain circumstances, the same

Developing the National Economy Title 105

The Significance of the Railway Goods Exhibition by Chen Yaozu 106

The establishment of railways in our country began in the late Qing Dynasty. In recent times, due to various influences such as political and military affairs, while there has been no significant progress, railways have their own missions and achievements in facilitating transportation and promoting cultural exchange. Therefore, industries such as agriculture, commerce, mining, etc., along the railway lines have made rapid progress in recent decades. However, the people of our country are limited in their knowledge and have not had the opportunity to examine them in detail. Although they talk about promoting domestic goods and resisting foreign goods, they do not know the source and quantity of domestic goods, nor the ways to promote and encourage them. As a result, goods are abandoned on the ground, people are idle, and national economy and people's livelihood are merely empty words, which is lamentable. This time, the Ministry of Railways has spent months collecting products from various railway lines across the country and exhibiting them publicly in a rotating manner for observation and inspection. By juxtaposing the good and the bad, people will know to encourage themselves. By displaying a variety of goods, buyers will be able to find supplies. This will make the people of our country realize that our nation is rich in resources and that it is not necessary to rely on imported goods to satisfy our needs for clothing, food, housing, and transportation. Its benefits to the national economy and people's livelihood are immeasurable. Furthermore, the exhibits this time include many agricultural and industrial products from the railway lines that have not been seen or heard of by the people of our country. The precision of their manufacturing and the abundance of their production are particularly unexpected. After this introduction, they will soon spread far and wide, selling well throughout the country along the railway tracks. Not only will farmers, merchants, and industrialists benefit, but railway transportation will also greatly increase. Therefore, I am happy to say a few words about it.

Photographs of Colleagues at the Railway Exhibition 107

The facilities are already in place. As for its operation, there is no possibility of exclusive control. Whether it is passenger or freight transport, all ships, sailboats, automobiles, carts, airplanes, and even cattle, horses, livestock, and all means of transportation can freely compete with trains. Therefore, railway operators, if they do not surpass other means of transportation in terms of speed, price, and service, will find it difficult to succeed. The operating methods of railway operators in our country are often passive, waiting for customers to come to their door, and yet they still have an unwelcoming attitude. Their arrogance is like corrupt officials and petty bureaucrats, and their extortion is like local tyrants and evil gentry. Therefore, merchants have no choice but to trade with trains and have to endure this unpleasantness. Moreover, in terms of transportation trends, highway construction is advancing rapidly, and long-distance buses are popular, so land transportation is sufficient to compete with trains. The abolition of likin and the removal of some restrictions on water transportation have led to the increasing prosperity of the shipping industry, so water transportation is also sufficient to compete with trains. The gradual expansion of aviation facilities means that air transportation is also sufficient to compete with trains. Therefore, it has been said that if railways want to maintain a considerable position in transportation in the future, they must strive to improve their own facilities and efficiency, and eliminate the arrogance of employees, as well as corrupt behavior. Furthermore, they must change their operating methods from a passive to an active position, and use various methods to attract customers widely. Otherwise, failure is inevitable. The Ministry of Railways' holding of a national railway line product exhibition has many implications, but it is undoubtedly one of the active operating methods. I hereby announce this to my railway colleagues on the opening day.

Therefore, our country's money is getting less and less, and the people are getting poorer and poorer. So, how does this phenomenon occur? The responsibility should be borne by three aspects: (A) Manufacturing factories cannot concentrate their efforts to achieve large-scale production, fail to cooperate, and compete with each other, cutting corners, and as a result, they all perish and cannot stand on their own. If this shortcoming can be corrected, production can be increased, quality can be improved, prices can be lowered, and cooperation can be strengthened to seek progress together. If we can first be self-sufficient, then foreign goods will not be able to resist self-made goods. Some unscrupulous merchants took the opportunity to rise up and acted without restraint. But can the patriotic spirit of all our citizens be suppressed by them? If everyone takes pride in using national goods and shame in mistakenly buying enemy goods, then it will not be difficult to eliminate foreign goods. Otherwise, without the Japanese destroying our country, our country itself will not be able to stand on its own." Railway Line Product Exhibition Opens Today 123

The exhibition is divided into thirteen categories

Products from all over the country participate

Yesterday, the press was invited to report on the significance of the exhibition

The National Railway Line Product Exhibition sponsored by the Ministry of Railways is scheduled to open at 2:00 PM today at the Zhonghua Xueyi Society on Avenue Dubail. Yesterday afternoon, the press was invited in advance to explain the significance of the Ministry of Railways holding this exhibition. The details are recorded as follows:

Overall Arrangement 124

The conference venue and the product exhibition area are fully arranged. The venue is also in the grand auditorium of the society, which has been newly decorated. From the gate, it is fully decorated with colorful arches. The product exhibition area is on the second floor and downstairs, and is arranged and numbered separately.

Representatives from All Parties 125

Vice Minister of Railways Zeng Zhongming and his wife took the night express train from Beijing last night and arrived in Shanghai this morning to attend the opening ceremony. It is also learned that the National Government has specially appointed Mayor Wu Tiecheng and the Executive Yuan has appointed its Secretary-General Chu Minyi as representatives to attend. Representatives from the City Chamber of Commerce, the National Federation of Commerce, and other groups will also participate on time.

Displayed Products 126

There are many kinds of products produced along the national railway lines. Due to time constraints, although it is not possible to collect and display them all, the number of products currently received and displayed is quite considerable, divided into thirteen categories: (1) Coal mines along the national railway lines, (2) Products from stations along the Jinpu Railway, (3) Products from stations along the Huhangyong Railway, (4) Products from stations along the Longhai Railway, (5) Products from stations along the Beining Railway, (6) Products from stations along the Pinghan Railway, (7) Products from stations along the Pingsui Railway, (8) Products from stations along the Guangzhou-Shaoguan section of the Yuehan Railway, with products from stations along the Guangzhou-Sanshui branch line, (9) Products from stations along the Xiang-E section of the Yuehan Railway, with products from stations along the Zhuping branch line, (10) Products from stations along the Zhengtai Railway, (11) Products from stations along the Daoqing Railway, (12) Products from stations along the Guangzhou-Kowloon Railway, and (13) Products from stations along the Nanxun Railway.

Sequential Exhibition 127

The exhibition is scheduled to open today and close on the 30th. After the closing, the products will be transported to Hankou for exhibition, and then transported to major ports such as Tianjin, Qingdao, and Guangzhou for exhibition in sequence, so that the national public has a deep understanding.

The True Meaning of the Railway Exhibition 128

Yu Yan, Director of the Business Department of the Ministry of Railways, received the press at the Zhonghua Juyi Society at 2:00 PM yesterday. More than 20 reporters from various newspapers attended. Director Yu first stood up and reported, followed by President Li Zhaohuan of Jiaotong University who delivered a speech. Director Yu reported that the true meaning of this railway exhibition is to display samples of products produced along the national railway lines for the general industrial and commercial circles to view. The comparison of these samples, as well as the value, freight, origin, sales market, seasons, transportation methods, taxes, and other issues, are all issues that general merchants want to solve in their minds. This association has specially made a simple report on its findings to provide merchants with research and reference for purchasing goods. This is the intention of this railway exhibition. The products produced along the railway lines are mostly domestic goods necessary for the daily life of the general public, such as agricultural products, mineral products, and industrial products, which are all goods transported by railways. According to the statistics of 1931, mineral products accounted for more than 13 million tons, accounting for 55.48% of the total national freight transport, followed by agricultural products, accounting for more than 5.2 million tons, accounting for 22.19% of the total national freight transport, and then industrial products, accounting for more than 3.5 million tons, accounting for 15.22% of the total national freight transport. These goods are transported to the market or destination by railway, and although the quantity is large, they are all very common rice, flour, cotton, medicinal materials, coal, coke, and other daily necessities. However, the products produced in different places are naturally the objects that general merchants urgently hope to view in detail. In essence, the better the samples, the easier it is to expand the sales market. However, although these samples are the objects of our exhibition today, we are not taking them out to show off novelty and victory. To expand the market for domestic products along the line, we naturally cannot passively let everything go. Regardless of the quality of the samples, we should try to promote the excellent ones and let them be sold as much as possible, and we should encourage the inferior ones to find ways to improve them. This exhibition is a vanguard for the general inland production class to promote and publicize, and it can also be said to break the first difficult hurdle for the majority of manufacturers who are relatively short of capital and unable to promote their products to distant places. This is the true meaning of the railway exhibition. At the same time, due to the expansion of the sales market for domestic products, the railway's own transportation business will naturally develop accordingly. Due to the development of the railway transportation business, the national economy along the line will become more developed. This is the ultimate goal of this railway exhibition. Although the railway is a state-run enterprise, its nature is actually a business organization that purely serves the people. The goods transported by the railway are to transport the raw materials or industrial products generally needed by the people's production enterprises along the line to the market or to the industrial area, so as to maintain the balance between production, consumption, and supply on all sides, and to adjust their deficiencies. This is the responsibility of the railway. In other words, if general merchants or manufacturers are looking for a large-scale, rapid transportation method that can shorten the distance and reduce the consumption of a long time, the most convenient way is to entrust the railway to transport goods. On the railway side, it can not only be responsible for shipping, but also transport large quantities of goods at cheap freight rates. Merchants can save money, and all responsibilities can be ignored. It will be transported to you on time, without any loss or omission. This is the responsibility of the railway to general merchants. Since the railway undertakes this major responsibility, it naturally directly reduces the burden on merchants, and at the same time reduces the cost of goods, and indirectly reduces the burden on the general consuming class in terms of purchase prices. At the same time, it increases the purchasing power of the general consuming class. The result of this kind of economic connection can directly promote the prosperity of the production business and increase the power of the Republic of China. In other words, it can increase the national strength to resist the enemy. Increasing strength is the only way to save ourselves.

Customs Installs Radio Beacons on Great Xu Island 129

Regular weather reports to begin on May 1

Hua Wu Shan Radio Beacon changes Broadcast time

In order to facilitate shipping, the Inspector General of Customs of Jianghai has specially added radio beacons to the Great Xu Island Lighthouse to report the weather at any time, so that ships can be prepared. In order to connect all the radio beacons, the broadcast time of the Hua Wu Shan radio beacon signal has also been changed. The two notices issued by the Maritime Section of the Jianghai Customs yesterday morning are recorded below:

Notice 1 130

Regarding the announcement: The Inspector General of Customs has ordered that a radio beacon should be installed at the Great Xu Island Lighthouse, which belongs to the Jianghai Customs, to facilitate navigation. All matters related to the installation of the beacon should be listed separately and ordered to the Surveyor of Works to comply with and handle. It should be complied with. A notice is hereby issued, and the orders are recorded below for the information of Chinese and foreign shipping merchants. This is hereby announced. The details are as follows: (1) Location of installation: Great Xu Island Lighthouse. (2) Date of installation: Around May 1 of this year. However, from May 1 to October 31 of this year, it is the trial period. The broadcast work may be interrupted during this period, and no further announcements will be made. In the future, after the trial period expires, the beacon will become a permanent installation, and no further announcements will be made. (3) Beacon information: The beacon uses intermittent radio waves with a wavelength of 1,000 meters. Its call sign is Z, which is transmitted according to the Morse code for 1 minute and 40 seconds. (4) Transmission time: When the weather is dark or foggy, the beacon signal is transmitted every six minutes, that is, the code (丨丨:丨丨:) is transmitted for 1 minute and 40 seconds, and the stop time is 4 minutes and 20 seconds. The above signals are transmitted according to the China coastal zone (i.e. 120 degrees east longitude) (5) Time: It is broadcast once every hour from 2 minutes, 8 minutes, 14 minutes, 20 minutes, and 26 minutes. In clear weather, it is broadcast twice every half hour, that is, the code (丨丨:丨丨:) is transmitted first for 1 minute and 40 seconds, the stop time is 4 minutes and 20 seconds, and then the code (丨丨:丨丨:) is transmitted for 1 minute and 40 seconds, and the stop time is 22 minutes and 20 seconds. The above signals are transmitted according to the China coastal zone (i.e. 120 degrees east longitude). Time: It is broadcast sequentially from 32 minutes every hour. (6) Other matters: The beacon will work in conjunction with the radio beacon set up at the Hua Wu Shan Lighthouse to facilitate navigation. (See Customs Tax Department Navigation Notice No. 1040) (7) Relevant maps: Waterway map No. 1011 of the Navy Department of the Republic of China.

Liang Shiyi Passed Away Yesterday 134

Suffered from heart disease after arriving in Shanghai and died despite medical treatment

The coffin will be transported back to Sanshui for burial this afternoon

His last words emphasized the people's livelihood

Liang Shiyi, who had long been highly regarded in the transportation and economic sectors, came to Shanghai a month ago in light of the loss of Rehe and the danger in North China, intending to go north to participate in the anti-Japanese war. After arriving in Shanghai, he suffered from heart disease and was admitted to Baolong Hospital for treatment. Recently, his condition worsened, and he passed away at 1:30 a.m. yesterday, at the age of sixty-five. The details of Liang's life and his condition during his illness are recorded below.

Arrived in Shanghai Last Month 135

Liang Shiyi held important positions throughout his life, but since returning to Guangdong in 1925, he had not been involved in worldly affairs, residing in Hong Kong or his ancestral home of Sanshui. It was not until the National Government convened a national crisis conference in January last year that Liang was invited and came to Shanghai. However, he happened to arrive during the January 28th Incident, so he stayed in Shanghai to assist in the anti-Japanese cause. In March, when the 19th Route Army withdrew, he returned to Guangdong. Last month, with the fall of Rehe Province and the crisis in North China, Liang felt uneasy in Hong Kong and resolutely went north again to assist the government and the anti-Japanese cause. He departed from Hong Kong on March 1st and arrived in Shanghai on March 3rd.

Treatment Process 136

After arriving in Shanghai, Liang Shiyi resided at his private residence on Haig Road, McTyeire Road. Liang caught a cold in late last month. His family intended to call a doctor for treatment, but Liang refused, saying, "We should not call a doctor for a mere cold. We

Liang Shiyi's posthumous portrait

should use a strong will to overcome the illness." Towards the end of the month, his condition gradually worsened, and his family insisted on sending him to the hospital. Liang did not strongly refuse at this point and was taken to Baolong Hospital on Meadville Road by his family on the first of this month, where he was treated by Dr. Boro, a German medical doctor. After Dr. Boro diagnosed Liang, he found that Liang's heart was enlarged and immediately gave him an injection to shrink it. On the 5th, Liang suddenly vomited two mouthfuls of fresh blood. At that time, Dr. Boro suspected a ruptured large blood vessel. On the 7th, it was proven that this was not the case and that there was accumulated blood in the stomach. Dr. Boro carefully treated him. By the 8th, his condition had greatly improved, and his family celebrated that Liang would recover. Unexpectedly, at 1:10 a.m. on the 9th, he suddenly fell into a coma and could not be saved. After Liang fell into a coma at 1:10 a.m. yesterday, he passed away at 1:30 a.m. Liang's younger brother, Shiyi, and more than ten children and relatives were by his side. Seeing his coma, they rushed to call doctors for emergency treatment, but it was too late. His family telegraphed the Universal Funeral Home to send a car to the hospital. His children transported Liang's remains to the car and returned directly to his private residence on McTyeire Road.

Condolences from Relatives and Friends 137

Liang's body was transported back to his private residence from Baolong Hospital and immediately given a small encoffining. The grand encoffining is scheduled for this afternoon, and the coffin will still need to be transported back to Sanshui, Guangdong, for burial. Yesterday, people from all walks of life in Shanghai and Liang's relatives and friends, upon hearing of Liang's death, visited Liang's residence to express their condolences. There were more than two hundred people, mostly from the banking and business sectors. Ye Gongchuo, the former Minister of Communications, also went to help with the funeral arrangements. Duan Qirui, who was living in seclusion in Shanghai, sent someone with a funeral gift to express his condolences. Yesterday, a shed had been erected in front of the house to prepare for the funeral in Shanghai.

Family Situation 138

Liang's wife is currently ill in Hong Kong. She was notified by telegram yesterday. Liang has four sons. The eldest son, who studied in the United States, is deceased. The second son, Dingji, is currently the manager of the Guangdong Shanghai Bank. The third son, Dingshu, is currently the special commissioner of the Ping-Sui Railway under the Ministry of Railways. The fourth son, Dingmin, is currently a radio engineer at the Guangdong Radio Station. He has three grandsons, all from his second son. He has six daughters. The eldest daughter, Haoyin, is married to Guan Zuzhang, currently the director of the Ping-Han Railway Engineering Office. The second daughter, Huaisheng, is married to Qu Jiyou, currently the deputy manager of the Tianjin Bank of Communications. The third daughter, Yusheng, is married to Guo Jinkun, who works in the Shanghai banking sector. The fourth daughter, Zangsheng, is married to Xiong Jingtang, who works in Peiping. The fifth daughter, Wosheng, is married to Li Kunhou, who works in Hong Kong. The sixth daughter, Yisheng, is unmarried and is currently in Hong Kong caring for her mother's illness. Liang also has a younger brother, Shiyu, who is currently working in Hong Kong.

Liang Shiyi's Last Words 139

During his illness, Liang was constantly concerned about the national crisis, saying that the nation had reached this point and that everyone must automatically work hard to find a glimmer of hope. He left his last words to his relatives and friends. The original text is recorded as follows: "The praise and criticism I have received in my life are countless, and I have never argued. I am confident that there must be someone in the world who deeply understands me. All my actions have always been in my heart. Although I am unwilling to display my achievements, the truth exists naturally. Those who comment on the world may be able to seek it in the facts. In 1911, I assisted Mr. Tang Shaoyi in supporting the Republic, and over the years, my plans and measures for foreign affairs are well known to my close friends. They are all related to historical materials, and I hope someone will record them. As for the economic and financial undertakings I created, although they are praised by the world, they are actually insignificant. I sincerely hope that colleagues in both fields can especially save the people's livelihood, otherwise, the future will be unimaginable."

Life Achievements 140

Liang, whose courtesy name was Yansun, was sixty-five years old and from Sanshui, Guangdong. He was a Jinshi in the Jiawu year of the late Qing Dynasty. He successively served as the principal of the Ministry of Justice in the abolished Qing Dynasty. At the end of the Guangxu era, he traveled to various countries with Tang Shaoyi. After returning to China, he served as the president of the Bank of Communications. After the establishment of the Republic, he served as the secretary-general of the Presidential Office and acting Minister of Finance. When Yuan secretly proclaimed himself Emperor Hongxian, Liang was the Chief of the General Staff. After Yuan's death, Liang went abroad for many years. After returning to China, he served as the Director-General of State Affairs, Speaker of the Senate, Chairman of the Financial Rehabilitation Committee, Chairman of the Financial Reorganization Committee, and member of the Customs Special Committee. Liang had a great relationship with the country. During the abolished Qing Dynasty, he made great efforts to develop transportation and was admired by the world. He made many contributions to the financial industry. During the Guangxu era, he was appreciated by Zhang Zhidong, the Governor-General of Huguang, and made great efforts to build railways and handle foreign affairs, gradually showing his talent. Later, he followed Tang Shaoyi to Tibet to handle British-Indian foreign affairs. He then worked in the Ministry of Posts and Communications, managing postal affairs and railway affairs. He repeatedly negotiated with various countries to purchase transportation materials, which was opposed by many Chinese people at the time. Liang did not care about public opinion and resolutely did it. As a result, various countries also admired Liang's character. Later, he served as the president of the bank, the director-general of the railway, and the director of the Constitutional Preparatory Bureau. When the revolution broke out, Liang advised the Qing Emperor to abdicate. At that time, the situation was very dangerous, but Liang was still able to resolutely advocate for it, which was praised by the Chinese people. When Yuan Shikai became president, Liang served as the Secretary-General of the Presidential Office and concurrently Minister of Communications. He was later transferred to Minister of Finance. During the era of Xu Shichang and Duan Qirui, Liang served as the Prime Minister and Chairman of the Finance Committee. At that time, Liang actively reorganized the finances and strongly supported customs autonomy. When Zhang Zuolin's forces were deployed in North China, Liang suggested stopping the civil war and implementing unification. Because it could not be implemented, he angrily returned to Guangdong. During the January 28th Shanghai War, Liang worked hard in Shanghai to prepare for assistance to the anti-Japanese cause. When the 19th Route Army withdrew, Liang returned to Guangdong. Recently, due to the fall of Rehe and the danger in North China, he came to Shanghai last month. When he arrived in Shanghai, he suffered from hemoptysis. The doctor ordered him to rest, but Liang, concerned about the country, could not follow the doctor's orders and passed away.

We have repeatedly called for these two things. Now, considering that the Central Government has a new opportunity to start anew with the people, we are making our previous suggestions again to jointly save the country from danger. The government and the people have been separated for a long time. To show sincerity in the hope of achieving national unity, please begin with this. We offer our sincere words and respectfully request your consideration. We hope that compatriots across the country will rise up together, reverse this crisis, and open a new path. Li Zhengwu Passed Away Yesterday 141

Passed away last night due to abdominal carbuncle

The grand encoffining is scheduled for tomorrow afternoon

Li Zhengwu, who was a revolutionary leader in the early years of the Republic of China, had been living in seclusion in Shanghai since his retirement. Recently, three months ago, Li suddenly suffered from stomach problems, with frequent severe pain. He immediately consulted various doctors for diagnosis and treatment, but with little effect. Since the end of last month, his condition worsened. Li decided to switch to Western medicine for treatment. Because his home was not suitable for his illness, he moved into Room 107 of the Sino-Western Sanatorium at 536 Route Paul Henry Villard on Sunday (the 2nd) of last week. He was treated by Dr. Macredie of the sanatorium, who diagnosed that the pain inside Li's body was not in the stomach but was due to a carbuncle in the lower abdomen, which could only be treated with surgery. After Li's family learned of this, they consulted Li himself and, with his consent, had the doctor perform the surgery at 8 a.m. on the 3rd. It was found that there was a considerable amount of pus in the lower abdomen, which was washed clean and sutured. The process was quite successful. However, because Li was old and his energy was insufficient, his condition suddenly changed the night before. Despite the best efforts of the doctors, it was difficult to see any effect. He passed away in the sanatorium at 9 p.m. yesterday, at the age of fifty-nine. Li's family entrusted the China Funeral Home to send a car to transport the remains back to Li's private residence at 19, Lane 52, Route Grand Occident at 10:30 p.m. that night. The grand encoffining is scheduled for 2 p.m. on the 11th. It is expected that there will be a grand funeral with plain carriages and white horses.
