Huang Jintao's Speech on Building the Central Steel Plant 143

丨Relationship with Industrial and National Defense丨

Director Huang Jintao of the Ministry of Industry delivered a valuable speech on the relationship between the Central Steel Plant and national defense at the specialized research conference of the Jiaotong University Industrial and Iron Exhibition. His speech stated that in today's discussion of national defense construction, the manufacture of military equipment should be considered the most important element. The military equipment manufacturing industry should be based on the development of all related industries before directly producing military equipment manufacturing plants to complete the so-called industries related to military equipment manufacturing. The following can be listed: steel, coal, petroleum, steel, lead-zinc, tungsten, antimony, aluminum, sulfur, nitrate, wood, rubber, sulfuric acid, nitric acid, chemical drugs, machinery, electrical, and other eighteen kinds. The cotton, wool, and grain used for military supplies are not included. The above industries are generally referred to as military industries. Military industries do not only refer to arsenals. All industries closely related to military affairs can be referred to as military industries. Those who directly manufacture military equipment are military industries, and the production of raw materials used for manufacturing military equipment should also be referred to as military industries. Before the European War, European and American countries tried their best to develop the above industries, but they only tended towards economic construction and commercial competition. After the countries joined the European War, the whole country was mobilized, and the above industries were directly transferred to the military equipment manufacturing industry. The needs of wartime should be prepared on a peacetime basis. According to recent statistics, the United States has 714 iron-smelting furnaces, Germany has 211 iron-smelting furnaces, and the United Kingdom has 187 iron-smelting furnaces. Japan has very little iron ore reserves, but there are 34 iron-smelting furnaces in the country, and the iron ore is purely taken from China. The reason why Japan must seize Manchuria is that once it obtains Manchuria, the source of iron ore and other raw materials for manufacturing steel can become increasingly stable. If we want to subdue Japan, we must first subdue it with economic policies. Before the Soviet Union implemented the Five-Year Plan, there were only about 70 iron-smelting furnaces in the country. After the success of the Five-Year Plan, it reached 103. It can be seen that the steel industry is important for the country's status and economic development. Each country's iron-smelting plant is also equipped with by-product coking furnaces, and many of the by-products are raw materials for manufacturing gunpowder. China currently has fewer than ten iron-smelting furnaces, large and small, and most of them are old or simple, and no by-product coking furnaces are attached to extract gunpowder raw materials. If we compare China's population with the number of steel consumed each year, the amount consumed per person is only one-two-hundredth of that of the United States. China currently consumes 600,000 tons of steel per year. If calculated according to the steel consumption rate of the United States, China would need 120 million tons of steel per year, which is one and a half times the world's steel production. According to recent statistics, the world's steel production is 94 million tons, of which the United States accounts for 45%, the United Kingdom accounts for 8%, Germany accounts for 15.5%, Japan only accounts for 1.5%, and other countries account for 30%. Therefore, based on the proportion of China's population to other countries, it should establish more iron-smelting furnaces and steel-making plants. Only when the steel industry is developed can all industries be developed accordingly, not to mention the relationship between national defense construction and the military industry. Currently, most of the raw materials required by China's arsenals are imported from foreign countries, and the degree of immaturity of its military industry is self-evident. Among the above-mentioned eighteen industries, the most difficult to establish and the most expensive are steel and oil. However, all military equipment is manufactured using steel as raw material. Therefore, steel occupies the most important position in the military industry and national defense construction. Establishing the foundation of the steel industry and attempting the independence of the steel industry should not be delayed for a day. Moreover, the steel industry is closely related to the transportation industry and other manufacturing industries. Here are the details of where steel is needed to manufacture all military equipment. Various guns, such as fortress guns, mountain guns, field guns, anti-aircraft guns, etc., have barrels made purely of Nickel-Chrome Steel or other Alloy Steel. The barrels of mortars are made of cast iron. Various guns, such as machine guns, heavy machine guns, rifles, box guns, submachine guns, pistols, etc., have barrels that are also made of Nickel-Chrome Steel or other Alloy Steel. Various gun carriages and gun accessories are made of ordinary steel (Carbon Steel) or Special Steel. Various bayonets are made of Tungsten Steel or Molybsenum Steel. The shells of fortress guns, mountain guns, and field guns are made of steel, brass, and lead, with steel being the most important part. Mortar shells are made of cast iron. Aircraft bombs are made of cast iron and brass, with cast iron accounting for the majority. In the manufacture of bullets, in addition to using copper, zinc, and lead, steel cups are also used. Tanks must be made of steel plates and other steel parts. Part of the aircraft must be made of Alloy Steel. The armor plate of warships is made of Chrome Steel, and other parts also require steel plates. Submarines must be made of steel plates. In summary, military equipment is almost entirely made of steel as an important raw material. Moreover, the by-products obtained from steel mills through coke production can be used to extract raw materials for gunpowder. In addition to developing ordinary industries, building a steel plant also means developing the military industry and the national defense industry. If you want all military equipment to be manufactured domestically, then building a steel plant will not be enough to produce all of the steel needed. China's military industry is still in its infancy. If we want to manufacture all military equipment, we may not be able to do so. The first step is to build a new-style steel plant to produce steel materials for military equipment in addition to supplying steel for industrial use, so as to build the foundation of national defense construction. If we want to combine this without establishing it, and only wait for the future to solve it, we will miss the opportunity and delay it. If things must be done, we should not be afraid of the difficulties and wait for the future. In short, for the sake of military equipment manufacturing, the construction of this steel plant cannot be delayed for a day. Or someone might say, since we want to build a steel plant, why not first reorganize and expand the existing Hanyang Iron Works? I don't know that the Hanyang Iron Works has become part of the collateral for the debts of the Hanyeping Company to the Japanese and cannot be freely disposed of by the government. Even if it can be freely disposed of, its furnace seats and machine parts have been used for many years and are already old-fashioned. It would also require a large investment to proceed, which is not economically sound. Moreover, the factory site has no room for expansion. As for the Longyan Iron Works in northern China, although a pig iron furnace has been built, it has not been fully completed. Even if a steel plant is added, the steel materials it produces can only be sold in the north. If it is transported south to the Yangtze River area or Fujian and Guangdong, the freight will be expensive and uneconomical. Therefore, the most urgent thing at present is to first build a new-style steel plant in the Yangtze River area. In the future, the steel materials produced can be used for the industry in the central part and can also be transported to the north and south without fear of stagnation. This is also the plan to concentrate the military industry. Or someone might say, the steel materials for manufacturing military equipment must be smelted by an Acid Siemens-Martin Furnace. If ordinary steel mills use the Baslc Martinprocesn to smelt steel, the steel materials are not suitable for guns and cannons. I don't know that the production of low-phosphorus pig iron or low-phosphorus iron ore in European and American countries is gradually decreasing. The smelting of military steel materials mostly uses ordinary pig iron to first smelt Semi-Steel in a basic Martin furnace, removing impurities such as sand phosphorus, and then pouring it into an acidic Martin furnace to smelt pure steel. Its quality is very clean and the same as acidic Martin steel. Therefore, the Ministry of Industry's steel plant plan is to add an acidic Martin furnace and a three-ton electric steel smelting furnace in the steel smelting plant, which can simultaneously produce special steel or alloy steel for manufacturing gun barrels. As for its production, it will depend on the amount of steel needed to manufacture weapons each year. The majority of the steel materials produced in the plant will still be ordinary steel to meet the needs of various industries, so as to still operate on the principle of business, and the principal and interest of the investment are effectively guaranteed, and a surplus can still be obtained, which is truly a win-win situation. As for the existing Hanyang Arsenal, although there is a small acidic Martin furnace, it has never been used and has become old and useless. Even if it is used one day, it will be necessary to purchase low-phosphorus pig iron from abroad, which is very uneconomical. As for the small steel smelting plant in the Shanghai Arsenal, it will also be dismantled due to the relocation of the arsenal. It would be more convenient to use the aforementioned heavy furnace steel smelting method in the currently planned steel plant to produce steel materials for the arsenal. The Ministry of Industry plans to establish a new-style steel plant in the central, northern, and southern parts of China, but it is not easy to raise such a huge amount of money at one time. Therefore, we will first start with the central steel plant, selecting a location near the capital to build the plant, which is the so-called central steel plant. The annual steel material production of the plant is set at 150,000 tons, which will be carried out in two parts and completed in four years. After the completion of each step of construction, more than 70,000 tons of steel material can be produced. In addition, the coal and ore production will be set at 3,000 tons per day. The source of raw materials, the steps to be taken, the quantity of products, and the capital, cost, and surplus of each item are described below. (Source of raw materials) The iron ore will be supplied by Dangtu and Fanchang in Anhui, and Phoenix Mountain in Nanjing. If it is not enough, it will be taken from Daye and Echeng in Hubei. The coking bituminous coal will be supplied by Suxian and Leijiagou coal mines in Anhui and Huaiyuan and Huainan coal mines. If it is not enough, it will be taken from Yixian in Shandong and Pingxiang in Jiangxi.

(Steps to be taken) It is divided into four years and carried out in two steps. The table is listed below.

Central Steel Plant 144

First year: Survey the factory site, operate iron ore and coal mines, and purchase and transport machine furnace materials

Second year: Complete a 250-ton pig iron furnace, two 50-ton steel smelting open-hearth furnaces, a coking furnace, a power plant, etc.

Third year: Complete a 200-ton Martin-style tilting furnace, a three-ton gas steel smelting furnace, a harmony furnace, a steel ingot rolling mill, a large and small rolling mill, a hammer steel mill, etc.

Fourth year: Add a 250-ton pig iron furnace, two 50-ton steel smelting open-hearth furnaces, a 200-ton Martin-style tilting furnace, a steel rail mill, a hook nail mill, a steel wire mill, a coking furnace, a power plant, a machine factory, etc.

First step Second step

Jiangsu People Initiate the Jiangsu Huai River Guiding Advancement Association Declaration of the Jiangsu Huai River Guiding Advancement Association 147

What is meant by "guiding the Huai"? It means guiding it into the sea. The Huai already enters the sea. Why guide it? Is it entering the sea after causing harm, or entering the sea after creating benefits? These are vastly different. "Guiding" means removing its harm and creating its benefits. Considering the benefits and harms of the past, its guidance should be expedited and must be promoted, hence the term "advancement." Considering the benefits and harms of the future, its guidance should be even better, and must be discussed, hence the term "association." The urgency and excellence of guiding the Huai should be planned by the authorities, but the benefits and harms of guiding the Huai are truly experienced by our people. To experience benefits and harms without being moved is not human nature. This is why this association is established. What is the scope of the association? It should be determined by the scope of the benefits and harms. The reach of benefits and harms can be direct or indirect. The need to remove harm and create benefits is equal in both cases. Speaking of direct benefits and harms, the Jiang (Yangtze), Huai, He (Yellow River), and Ji were anciently called the "four independent rivers." "Independent" means flowing independently into the sea, so there was little harm. Since the Yellow River diverted the Huai's flow, the Huai River's path to the sea has been blocked. Blocked, it then enters the Yangtze. The Yangtze's strength is greater than the Huai's. The Huai cannot overcome the Yangtze and freely enter the sea, so the Huai's water becomes full and causes harm. In Anhui, it affects Lu, Feng, Ying, and Si; in Jiangsu, it affects Huai and Yang. In 1931, the Huai River overflowed in Anhui, and the Grand Canal breached in Jiangsu. The entire Huai River basin was spared, which is the most prominent example of its harm. Therefore, if the Huai River independently flows into the Yangtze River and the sea, the harm will be moderate, but if it enters the sea, the harm will be great, which is what is meant by "entering the sea after causing harm." This is the direct harm. The Huai is a clear-flowing river, suitable for irrigation and transportation, like the Yangtze. Its flow is sufficient to supply the farmland and waterways of the entire 2,000-mile Huai River basin, inexhaustibly. Today, only a dozen or so counties in Huai and Yang benefit, accounting for only one or two tenths of the Huai's water. The remaining eight or nine tenths are abandoned into the Yangtze, treated as waste. If it could all be utilized, the benefits would be unimaginable. This is the direct benefit. Furthermore, speaking of indirect benefits and harms, the reason the Yangtze can accommodate many flows is not in the Yangtze itself, but in the lakes along the Yangtze. Today, the gullies above Chongqing are already filled with rocks and sediment, becoming flat land over time. Of the lakes below Wuhan, seven or eight tenths have transitioned from fishing and animal husbandry to farming. Based on the difference between the high and low water levels of the Yangtze in the past twenty years, its water storage capacity is far less than before. Therefore, in 1921 and 1931, Hankou and Nanjing were flooded, reaching depths of over ten feet and receding for a month. Gaochun and Dongba almost collapsed. When the Yangtze is at its peak, it is also the time of the Huai's floods, which has been proven repeatedly. Above Zhenjiang, the Yangtze is confined by mountains and cannot expand. Even the Yangtze's channel below Jin and Jiao is limited. The ports of Chongming and Wusong are accumulating sediment and are not draining well. The Yangtze's discharge capacity is already struggling to cope. If a way is found to raise the Huai's water level and compete with the Yangtze, the Yangtze's flow will be impeded, inevitably overflowing between Nanjing and Wuhu. Then Gaochun's Dongba Dam and Gaoyou's Grand Canal embankment face the same danger: either breach the Grand Canal embankment to release the Huai, or breach the Dongba Dam to release the Yangtze. If the Yangtze breaches eastward, the Tai Lake basin will be even worse than the 1931 Huaiyang disaster. This is the inevitable trend of water, and the terrain is inescapable. Even if it is spared, the banks of the Yangtze will not be spared. This is the indirect harm to Jiangnan, Nanjing, Zhenjiang, Suzhou, Changzhou, Songjiang, and Taicang. As for the Yi and Si rivers, they are inherently no match for the Huai. If the Huai has nowhere to go, the tailwaters of the Yi and Si will also be blocked, inevitably collapsing in the central Grand Canal basin, causing harm to Xuzhou and Haizhou. In 1931, the inner Grand Canal and the central Grand Canal simultaneously breached, and the disaster in Xuzhou and Haizhou was equal to that in Huaiyang. The reason lies in this. This is also the clear indirect harm of the Huai to Xuzhou and Haizhou. However, the indirect harm to Xuzhou and Haizhou is already a common sight, while the indirect harm to Nanjing, Zhenjiang, Suzhou, Changzhou, Songjiang, and Taicang is only a future potential threat, so fewer people pay attention. However, the old course of the Yangtze below Wuhu is the direct upstream of Tai Lake, and its embankment is at Gaochun's Dongba Dam. In 1931, the Yangtze River already gave a serious warning. This indirect scope of harm extends to the entire province of Jiangsu. In the past, when the Yellow River flowed south, the Huai was weak and the Yellow River was strong, unable to cross the Yellow River and find its way to the sea. It had to seek accommodation between the Yangtze and Yellow rivers, hence the system of ten dams returning to the Yangtze and five dams emptying into the sea, causing the human benefits of a large amount of clear water to become harmful water. Today, the Yellow River has moved north, and the Huai has ample space to enter the sea. Moreover, the Longhai Railway is the only trunk line spanning Asia, with the potential to connect to the European continent in the west and the Pacific shipping lanes in the east. Northern Jiangsu, at this junction of land and sea, must have a large commercial port to utilize this connection. However, freshwater is still lacking. This vast plain of 2,000 miles stretching south to Anhui, north to Jiangbei, and its tens of millions of people, also urgently need to use the production of the Huai River to connect with that commercial port day and night, thereby establishing a relationship with the world economy. The Huai, in addition to providing water to benefit the farmland of Huaiyang, should still be supplied as before. The remaining surplus water, which serves no purpose, seems to be able to be transformed from waste to good, to compensate for the value of our engineering consumption. If this plan of benefiting the people through benefits can be researched and achieved, the scope of indirect benefits will certainly not be limited to provincial boundaries. This is what is meant by "entering the sea after creating benefits." However, as this is the beginning of organizing a research group, it is not necessary to excessively expand the scope without boundaries. The people of Anhui have already established this association first, and their views on the benefits and harms of the Huai, and the means they hold to remove harm and create benefits, are not much different from those of our province. Therefore, we specifically cite this precedent and tentatively organize this association within the scope of the province to collect old news and seek new meanings, consult and exchange with all relevant parties, to help the Huai River guiding authorities gather ideas and increase benefits. We also hope that before the Huai River guiding authorities make a decision, they will be sincere and public with our people regarding the known benefits and harms of the past and the foreseeable benefits and harms of the future, so that our people can gradually understand, entrust their hearts and trust, and unite to achieve what is called "many hands make light work, many minds build a strong wall." This is the meaning of this association's "advancement." We respectfully present this idea to our fellow villagers, and attach the articles of association (omitted) to solicit like-minded people. Initiators: Gu Zhuxuan, Chen Bomeng, Shen Ziping, Zhu Shaowen, Ji Longtu, Cheng Xiechun, Yang Ruiwen, Hu Xianbo, Chen Chaobi, Gong Qi.

Telegram Against Diverting the Yellow River into the Huai River 148

To all newspaper offices, the National Government Executive Yuan, the Ministry of Interior, the Huai River Guiding Committee, the Yangtze River Committee, the governments of Jiangsu, Anhui, Zhejiang, Jiangxi, Hubei, and Henan: According to the Anhui Tianjin Fellow Association, the Henan Construction Department recently planned to divert the Yellow River from below Rongze into the Jialu River (southern Henan), through the Dasha River (northern Anhui), and then into the Huai River and the Yangtze River. Also, reading the Nine Days Newspaper, the Huai River Guiding Committee made some explanations to the people of Anhui who opposed diverting the Yellow River into the Huai River, saying that this move would not harm Anhui. It seems that the matter is inevitable. But if so, it would harm the Huai, harm the Yangtze, harm the Grand Canal, and harm the source of the national and people's economy. The Yellow River has been a harmful water in the Central Plains of our country for thousands of years. The source of the Yellow River is more than 13,800 feet above sea level. Above Mengjin, the mountain ranges on both sides are close together, and the water quality is still clear, so it is not very harmful. Below Rongze, the loose soil of the plains is eroded by the rapid currents, carrying sediment downstream, which inevitably causes siltation over time, with the most changes, and there will be problems every hundred years. This is the general situation. The method of Yu the Great in controlling the waters was to divide them. First, he divided the Yangtze, Huai, Yellow River, and Ji into four independent rivers, each flowing independently into the sea, which was to prevent them from combining and harming each other. And the method of governing the Yellow River was to divide it into nine in its lower reaches, turning the trunk into branches. This is the opposite of the method of governing the Yangtze and Huai rivers, which is to gather the branches into the trunk to enter the sea. Still, he did not think it was enough and devoted himself to the streams, ditches, and canals to divide them finely, so that the fields everywhere had a place to hold water, and the people could enjoy the benefits of water without suffering its harm. Therefore, Gun was an ancient engineer, and Yu was an ancient water conservancy expert. Because he controlled the water as a water conservancy expert, his purpose and means were able to transcend the scope of water and not be confined to the limits of water. Therefore, he could utilize water without being used by water. In later generations, Yellow River and sea engineering belonged to the central government, and farmland water conservancy was the responsibility of the local government. Since the functions were divided, the purposes were different. The central governments of past dynasties governed the Yellow River as engineers, and their focus was only on the prevention of the Yellow River itself, and not on other methods of accommodating it. Over time, they only knew that streams, ditches, and canals were the path for draining rainwater into the giant river, and forgot that they had the function of dividing the land and distributing water to the fields. In the vast Central Plains, except for the rice-producing areas, the legacy of ditches and canals has disappeared. As a result, the Yellow River's disaster has never ceased. This is clear evidence that governing the Yellow River should be divided and not combined. The Yangtze and Huai river basins have sticky soil and clear water, and the lakes can exist permanently as natural water storage devices. Diverting water into the lakes is enough to reduce the anger of the water, and the land is suitable for rice cultivation, so irrigation requires many ditches and canals, and the capacity is naturally large. The Yellow River, on the other hand, has loose sand and muddy water, and lakes near the Yellow River cannot exist. Creating lakes on wasteland is impossible, and digging lakes is impossible. Only the system of streams, ditches, and canals can replace them, and allow farmland utilization to exist permanently. The difference between Gun and Yu lies in this. Otherwise, the Yellow River basin is not a widespread rice-growing area, and the rainfall in the northwest is not as great as in the southeast. Why did the well-field system and the ditch and canal system decline only after three dynasties and two thousand years? There must be something immortal about it. The Construction Department has the functions of both Yellow River and sea engineering and farmland water conservancy. It should plan comprehensively to make the Yellow River's water divided and beneficial, and should not make it combined and harmful. This is speaking of the benefits and harms of the Yellow River itself. Since the Song and Yuan dynasties, diverting the Yellow River into Bian caused Bian to be blocked, diverting the Yellow River into the Si caused the lakes of the Si to dry up, and diverting the Yellow River into the Huai caused the lower reaches of the Huai to be silted up. Today, the Huai has nowhere to go, causing harm to Ying, Feng, Hao, Si, Huai, and Yang. The reason for waiting for guidance and treatment is the disease of the Yellow River and Huai rivers joining. Moreover, the areas with long coastlines in the world are the places where culture and economy originated. Only our Huaihai region connects three provinces, occupying more than 600 miles of coastline, but its culture and economy are no different from the hinterland. This is also due to the Yellow River sand flowing down and the sea tides rising up, resulting in high beaches and shallow water, losing its coastline efficiency. Therefore, the coast of northern Jiangsu cannot only not compete with the coastlines of the world, but it is also far inferior to the seas of Shanghai, Tianjin, Shandong, Zhejiang, Fujian, and Guangdong. Fortunately, the tailwaters of the Yangtze River are still a major global port for navigation. If the Yellow River is diverted into the Huai River to the right, it will inevitably enter the sea through the Yangtze River, then the north and south of the Wusongkou will be full of sandy islands, all becoming flat land, and the Shanghai Sea will not be navigable. If the lower reaches of the Yangtze River are blocked due to siltation, then the area between Wuhu and Jinling will inevitably be full, collapsing the Dongba Dam, entering Tai Lake, and seeking another downstream Qian Tang River to flow into the sea. Since the Yellow River occupies the Huai River channel, the vast plain of northern Anhui and southern Huai will have no banks, and the floods will overflow freely, with nowhere to go. The largest plain in our country, except for the desert, that is sufficient to be a farming area is Liaoning, Jilin, and Rehe in the north, and Anhui, Henan, Jiangsu, and Zhejiang in the south. Now, the one in the north has been invaded by strong neighbors, leaving only this small remaining fruit, and destroying it ourselves. Where will the foundation of national wealth and the people's economy be entrusted? This is also about the benefits and harms of the Yangtze, Huai, coast, and the nation and the people. I believe that those who govern the water should consider the entire benefits and harms of the water before deciding on their policy. They must judge it with the knowledge of a water conservancy expert, and not just with the knowledge of an engineer. Governing water is a political matter, not just a technical matter. To see the small and not see the big will inevitably harm the matter. Our association is a water conservancy research organization. Because the benefits and harms are closely related, we dare not sacrifice the lives and property of tens of millions of people on the plains of the lower reaches of the Huai River for the Henan Construction Department to conduct Yellow River control experiments. Therefore, we dare to offer our views and humbly request a speedy halt to the Henan province's plan, and we are eagerly awaiting orders. The Jiangsu Huai River Guiding Advancement Association kowtows, respectfully.

Hua Sannan Accuses Ling Yian of Obstructing Public Morality and Abandonment 156

Appeal Sent Back for Retrial by the Third Branch of the High Court

Ling Hua, also known as Hua Sannan, a young woman from Dangkou, Suzhou, who formerly resided at No. 4 Deyi Lane, Tangjiawan, Ximen, is now 25 years old. On the evening of July 13, 1927 (when she was 19 years old), she took a neighboring child to the French Park in Gujiazhai to watch the French National Day memorial lantern festival. In the park, she met Ling Yian, a local man of about the same age as her, who currently resides at No. 33 Boxiang Village, Rue Luthy, and works as a clerk in the paint department of the De Fu Foreign Firm on the Jiangxi Road, Zhejiang Industrial Bank building. After talking, they learned that she was a young unmarried woman and he was also unmarried. They fell in love at first sight and wanted to become husband and wife. They soon had physical relations. Hua urged Ling to hire a matchmaker and after reaching an agreement, they began to live together without a wedding ceremony. After living together, their love grew deeper, and they had a son and a daughter, both of whom died young due to illness. Until April of last year, Ling became acquainted with a woman named Wang, and the couple's relationship gradually cooled down, and quarrels often arose. Ling then sent Hua back to her parents' home and abandoned her. She hired a matchmaker to negotiate with Ling, but to no avail. Therefore, she hired lawyer Zhao Zuwei to file a complaint with the criminal court of the Second Special Court, accusing Ling of obstructing public morals and abandonment, requesting an investigation, and attaching a civil lawsuit to recover losses of 5,000 yuan. The court, according to the complaint, opened a hearing on the eighth of last month to summon the defendant, Ling Yian, who also hired lawyer Zhu Dianqing to defend him. Because both sides admitted their relationship as husband and wife, but had not been married, the court ruled that the relationship of husband and wife was not in accordance with the criminal procedure of self-prosecution, and the court ruled that the case would not be accepted. The situation has been reported in previous newspapers. Now, Hua is dissatisfied with the original judgment and appealed to the Third Branch of the High Court. The trial was reopened by Judge Zhou, along with judges Guo and Fan, and Prosecutor Zhang. After summoning the two sides for argument, the court announced the end of the debate the day before yesterday and ruled to overturn the original judgment. The case should be tried by the Shanghai Second Special District Court. The case has been sent back to the original trial court by the High Court, and the trial will be reopened soon to summon both parties for retrial. At that time, the lawyers on both sides will surely have a fierce debate.

The day before yesterday, he went to the Chenjiahang riverside of the southern Huangpu River and jumped into the river. Renfeng Cloth Store on Avenue Edward VII Bombed Last Night 159

Only the Storefront Window and Some Cloth Were Destroyed

The Assailant Reportedly Wore Student Attire

Renfeng Cotton Cloth and General Merchandise Store, located at Nos. 339-341 Avenue Edward VII, at the intersection of Rue du Moulin, is one of the major general merchandise and cloth stores on Rue du Consulat in the French Concession. It is currently in its grand opening and offering large discounts, and business is even more prosperous. At 7:30 PM last night, someone suddenly threw a hand-pulled grenade into the store from the center of the eastern road. The sound of the explosion shook the neighborhood. Fortunately, all the store employees were having dinner in the back at the time, leaving only one or two people to guard the store, so no one was injured. By the time everyone rushed out, the grenade thrower had already disappeared without a trace. At the same time, the nearby Grand Stand Clock Police Station heard the news and dispatched Chinese and Western detectives to investigate. The investigation revealed that one side of the display window had been destroyed, six bolts of Hengzi brand high-quality fine twill fabric from the Wuxi Meiheng Factory had been damaged, eight bolts of bleached cloth from the brands of Fair, Yuanfang, Yihuo, and Taihe had been damaged, and five bolts of domestic silk crepe had been damaged. Several pieces of shattered grenade shells were collected and taken to the police station for investigation. Afterwards, according to witnesses in the vicinity, the grenade thrower was a young man in student attire. After throwing the grenade, he fled south towards MinGuo Road.

American Soldier's Drunken Brawl Results in Bloodshed 160

Wounded Soldier Sent to Lester Chinese Hospital for Treatment

Perpetrator Fled the Scene but Was Subsequently Arrested

At approximately 9 PM last night, two U.S. Marine Corps soldiers arrived at the Far Eastern Hotel at the intersection of Xizang Road and Guangdong Road seeking lodging. The hotel's cashier assigned them Room 111. The soldiers paid the room fee on the spot. Around 10 PM, four more soldiers from the same unit arrived, carrying a case of beer. The six soldiers then opened the case and began drinking and making merry in the room. In less than three hours, all the soldiers were heavily intoxicated, with beer bottles scattered all over the table. Unexpectedly, two of the soldiers suddenly disagreed and began arguing, which quickly escalated into a physical fight. One soldier, unable to withstand the other's force, drew his bayonet and repeatedly stabbed the other soldier, inflicting over ten wounds to his upper and lower body. The four soldiers present immediately rushed forward to try to disarm the assailant, but he turned and fled the room. The soldier ran aimlessly in several directions before finally identifying the main entrance and escaping. The hotel cashier, having learned of the incident, promptly reported it to the police. A police ambulance and a large number of detectives were dispatched. They first transported the injured soldier to Lester Chinese Hospital for treatment, and then detained the remaining four soldiers, along with the beer bottles and case, taking them all to the police station. After questioning, they were handed over to their commanding officer for further action. It was later learned that the fleeing assailant had also been apprehended by his unit.

Two Bags of Morphine Hidden in Shoe Soles 161

| Over One Hundred Ounces of Morphine Seized in Total |

Director Wen of the Shanghai Municipal Police Bureau, acting on a tip received the day before yesterday, learned that Wang Yaozhou, a native of Shaoxing, who operated the Lao Wang Zhengxing drum shop at No. 182 Fangbang Road in the city, was secretly running a large-scale morphine drug operation, specializing in the trafficking and sale of various narcotics. Consequently, at approximately 9 PM that evening, he dispatched Inspector Zheng Tingwei of the Inspection Department to the Second Precinct of the First District to request assistance in the investigation. Director Liu of the precinct then led Sergeant Li Fuyi and others to the Lao Wang Zhengxing drum shop, first surrounding the premises to prevent anyone from entering or leaving. They then entered the premises and conducted a search of the lower floor of the east building, but found no contraband. They immediately went upstairs to continue the search and soon discovered the illicit operation in a dark, small room on the rear floor. They found a tin basin containing white morphine, as well as four tin cans, each about a foot long and the diameter of a silver dollar, sealed at both ends with iron sheets. Upon opening them, they found that they also contained morphine. Shortly thereafter, they noticed a pair of leather shoes placed under a table. Upon closer inspection, they discovered that the shoes had false soles. They pried open the false soles and found two bags of morphine hidden inside. The total weight of all the morphine seized was estimated to be over one hundred ounces. They then searched the bedrooms of Wang's family members and found two rifles, both manufactured by the Hanyang Arsenal, a bayonet, one Mauser pistol bullet, one ammunition belt, and nine rifle bullets. However, the shop owner, Wang Yaozhou, had already fled upon hearing the news. His son, Wang Zijin, was detained, along with four others found in the room: Xu Jintian from Shandong, Zhang Gengqing from Henan, Liu Xikui from Danyang, and Chuan Rongsheng from Ningbo. All the evidence seized was brought to the police station. During preliminary questioning by Director Liu, the suspects gave evasive and contradictory statements, shifting blame among themselves. Considering the gravity of the matter, he ordered that a written report be prepared and that the suspects and witnesses be handed over to the Municipal Police Bureau for further investigation.

National Goods Discount Market Opens Yesterday 162

The National Goods Discount Market, established by the Shanghai National Goods Trading Company on Nanjing Road to counter the dumping of Japanese goods, opened yesterday. Patriotic citizens flocked to it, creating an unprecedented record. Total sales for the day, up to 7 PM, reached over 20,000 yuan. It was reported that by 12 PM, total sales were only over 4,000 yuan, but the crowds of shoppers were already exceptionally dense. From 2 PM onwards, the number of shoppers surged like a tide, resulting in sales exceeding four times the earlier figure. The shop assistants were overwhelmed with work. Among the goods sold, the largest quantities were silks and cotton fabrics, thermos flasks priced at seven jiao each, and rubber overshoes priced at five jiao per pair.

A Well-Dressed Swindler 164

Impersonating Court Personnel to Investigate Cases

Daring to Defraud Parties of Investigation Fees

| Swindler Displays Extravagance, Riding in a Chartered Car |

Shanghai is a place where people from all walks of life gather, and good and bad are mixed together. Deceitful and fraudulent activities occur frequently. Recently, a type of middle-class or upper-class rogue, dressed impeccably, has been impersonating investigators dispatched by the court to defraud parties of investigation fees. It so happened that the wife of Hu A'hong, Hu Yuan, who lived on Rue Tenant de la Tour in the French Concession, previously asked her old neighbor, Lu Jintao, to introduce business to her nephew. Lu, coveting Hu Yuan's beauty and money, attempted to seduce her unsuccessfully. Lu then falsely claimed that the business introduction had been successful and lured Hu Yuan to a lodging near Caojiadu shoe factory under the pretext of discussing the matter. There, Lu forcibly raped her. Subsequently, Lu often took advantage of Hu Yuan's husband's absence at work to arrange secret rendezvous and extort money from her for lavish spending. As time passed, Lu went a step further, demanding that Hu Yuan divorce her husband and live with him. When she refused, Lu learned of her husband's hospitalization and tricked Hu Yuan's brother into coming to Shanghai. Lu then confined and monitored the siblings, forcing them to sign a divorce agreement, threatening to kill them otherwise. Unable to endure the pressure, Hu Yuan pretended to agree and signed the document, regaining her freedom. She immediately hired a lawyer to file a lawsuit in the Criminal Division of the Second Special District Court, accusing Lu of obstructing her freedom and requesting an investigation and the revocation of the document. When the court summoned Lu based on the lawsuit, he had already fled upon hearing the news, and the hearing was rescheduled, as reported in previous newspapers. On the afternoon of the third of this month, Hu Yuan found Lu and brought him to the court. After the court held a hearing, Lu hired a lawyer who posted bail and secured his release pending further hearings. Unexpectedly, during this time, a well-dressed swindler, dressed in a Western suit and riding in a chartered car, claiming to be dispatched by the court to investigate the facts, visited Hu Yuan's home. Hu Yuan, unaware of the deception, truthfully recounted the events to the swindler. The swindler then told her that he could help her but required half of the investigation fee and transportation costs, totaling twelve yuan. Hu Yuan, not suspecting anything, gathered the money and gave it to him. The day before yesterday, when the hearing resumed, the defendant was represented by a lawyer. The plaintiff, Hu Yuan, also appeared in court with her lawyer and recounted the facts. She mentioned that someone claiming to be from the court had come to investigate and had taken the investigation fee. The judge, upon hearing this, was astonished and told Hu Yuan that the court had not sent anyone to investigate and that the visitor must have been a swindler. He advised her to be vigilant and, if she encountered him, to immediately bring him to the court for questioning. He also instructed that the case required investigation by the police station and that the defendant had failed to appear again, so the hearing would be postponed and a summons issued again. The judge instructed the defendant's lawyer to ensure the defendant's presence at the next hearing, or else he would be arrested. With that, the court adjourned. Only then did Hu Yuan realize that she had been deceived by a swindler. She immediately searched the audience seats in the courtroom but could not find the swindler anywhere. She then returned home dejectedly.

Method for Converting to Yuan, based on a conversion rate of 0.715. Upon receiving the reply, the Federation immediately notified the citizens within the district, issuing a notice stating: "Regarding the matter of notification, it has been found that various taxes and levies in this district have traditionally been calculated in silver taels, and tax collectors often do not convert them at the current market rate. The citizens of this district have felt greatly inconvenienced by this. Although the individual losses may seem small, they accumulate over time to a significant amount. Now that the National Government has officially ordered the abolition of taels and the adoption of yuan, this order must be obeyed. A letter was sent to the French Concession Municipal Council, and the Council has now issued a joint reply from the Superintendent and General Manager, translated as follows: 'We have received your letter of March 16th, stating that taxes and levies within the concession have traditionally been calculated in silver taels, and tax collectors often do not convert them at the current market rate. Now that the National Government has officially ordered the abolition of taels and the adoption of yuan, you request that we instruct the Tax Bureau to unanimously comply. We have carefully considered this matter. We acknowledge your Federation's deep concern for the interests of the citizens. We have decided to implement the method of abolishing taels and adopting yuan, based on a conversion rate of 0.715, effective April 1st, and have notified the Tax Bureau to comply accordingly.' In light of this, since the Municipal Council has decided on the method for converting silver to yuan, effective April 1st, citizens of this district may henceforth pay various taxes and levies based on the conversion rate of 0.715. This notice is hereby issued to all citizens of the district for their information." This notice is issued.

Pediatric and Gynecology Expert Dr. Chen Xizhi Practices Medicine in Shanghai Ms. Chen Xizhi, a native of Jiangsu and Shanghai, went to the University of Vienna in Austria at her own expense in the spring of 1927 to specialize in pediatrics and gynecology. She graduated in 1931, earning a doctorate in medicine. After returning to China, she practiced medicine in Shenyang and served as a professor and school doctor at Feng Yong University. After the September 18th Incident, she moved to Beijing to practice medicine. She has extensive clinical experience and is highly regarded by all sectors of society. It is reported that Ms. Chen recently returned to Shanghai and decided to practice medicine and help patients at the Nanyang Pharmacy at the entrance of Hongmiao Lane on Nanjing Road.

Letters to the Editor 169

To the Esteemed Editor, Upon reading yesterday's report in the "Local News" section of your newspaper, which stated that "a strike by fashion industry workers was triggered by Jin Taixiang shop owner Hu Jinhai's violation of the agreement, resulting in the payment of only ten cents per piece," I was greatly surprised. During the strike, some of the striking workers came to the shop and invited others to join the strike. At that time, I was not in the shop, and I do not know how, but a fight broke out between the workers, and they were arrested and sent to the police station. Afterward, the police summoned me for questioning and asked if I wanted to prosecute the workers for disturbing business. I did not want the workers to be implicated and replied that I requested that they be spared prosecution. However, the police did not grant my request and transferred the case to the court. These facts can be verified by those present at the scene. Regarding the issue of wages, the Social Bureau mediated and decided to increase the wages. Our shop followed this decision by adding ten cents per piece to the wages at the end of January. How can it be said that we violated the decision of the Party and government organs? Furthermore, our shop's workers have no complaints. I am afraid that the reports are inaccurate and hastily request that you make a correction. Respectfully, Hu Jinhai of Jin Taixiang, April 9th, 1933.

To the Esteemed Editor, Upon reading your newspaper's news on the 8th, regarding "Japanese ruffians causing trouble at the Luban Daolida Silk Factory," this is entirely untrue. Zhang Zhipeng is not an employee of our distribution office, but rather a friend. On that day, he was visiting Longhua with a Japanese friend, and they passed by our factory and stopped in for a brief visit. They left shortly after, and there was no trouble caused. This matter has absolutely no connection to our factory. I am deeply afraid that the outside world will misunderstand the truth, which would affect our factory's reputation. I request that your newspaper immediately make a correction. Sincerely, Dongya Silk Weaving Factory, April 9th.

To the Esteemed Editor, I was quite surprised to read the report in your newspaper's evening edition regarding "a strike by all the workers in the third department of the Yi Yuan Factory." The facts stated in the report are quite different from the truth. Our factory dismissed four casual workers who mend shoes - Cai Richu, Li Rongjiang, Dehua, and Yang Jia - for violating factory rules. These four individuals held grudges and coerced the workers to strike. Fortunately, the workers understood the importance of the situation and continued to work as usual. There was no strike or detention of workers. Seeing that their scheme had failed, the four individuals fabricated a report of a strike, attempting to confuse public opinion. The outside world is unaware of the truth, and I am deeply afraid that members of society will misunderstand the situation. Therefore, I specially write to your newspaper to request a correction. Respectfully, Shanghai Yi Yuan Elm Bark Manufacturing Factory, April 9th.

Readers' Advisory

Regarding the Discussion Letters on the Question of "Can One Return to the Countryside?" 171

(Two) Letter from Zhang Meijun of this City

Because of the economic bankruptcy of the countryside, a large number of laborers and intellectuals unable to make a living flow into the cities. Moreover, due to the commercial contraction in the cities, those who cannot find work, as well as those who have lost their jobs, are thinking of returning to the countryside in large numbers. Thus, the question of "Can One Return to the Countryside?" is raised. This is an overall social problem, not one that can be solved by isolated individuals. If one does not consider it from the perspective of the entire society but only from a personal viewpoint, one will inevitably encounter a dead end. Therefore, after reading Mr. You Huaigao, who has "always been enthusiastically advocating rural education to save the country," in response to Mr. Xiongsheng's letter, I have the following questions: (1) Mr. Huaigao said that the prerequisites for going to the countryside are: 1. Do you love the countryside? 2. Do you sincerely love your rural farmer friends? 3. Are you determined to work hard to make a living in the countryside? If these are the prerequisites, then we must recognize that the people who now want to return to the countryside originally came out of the countryside because they "do not love the countryside," "do not love the rural farmer friends," and "cannot endure hard work to make a living in the countryside." They are entirely motivated by a desire for ease and laziness, rather than being driven out by economic oppression in the countryside. At the same time, it can also be said that Mr. Xiongsheng wants to return to the countryside because he does not love the city, etc. This is completely detached from reality and will not find a way to solve the problem. (2) "The only way out for the intellectual class is to undertake the education of the countryside and the revitalization of the countryside." This is correct, but how to educate and revitalize? I want to educate, but first I must study the reasons why it cannot be educated. Naturally, this cannot be attributed to a lack of educational talents, or to the fact that people who are capable of education do not love the countryside... Similarly, to revitalize the countryside, we must first study the reasons for its destruction. Only gilded doctors would say that the destruction of the countryside is not due to imperialist aggression but due to "stupidity," due to not knowing "organization" such as cooperatives. If the causes of destruction are not removed, it is like water flooding the fields, not repairing the dikes, but only drawing water. Naturally, it is labor without effect. There was a gentleman in Changsha who worked hard in rural education, using his energy and the salary he earned from teaching on this school. As a result, the educational achievements were […], revitalization was out of the question, and the bankruptcy of the rural area there deepened with the trend, and it did not ease up because there was such a hardworking person there. This old gentleman only woke up in his sixties and has now abandoned his school. […], his school is exactly the same as or even better than what Mr. Huaigao envisions. […], he resolutely participated in the so-called overall reform movement. Therefore, I dare say that this kind of New Village movement is not the way out. It does not transform the entire life of the countryside, so naturally individual life and, as Mr. Huaigai said, "you are the leader of a village, you can carry out village governance work," cannot be realized. (3) Mr. Huaigao only pays attention to the issue of the intellectual class returning to the countryside, that is, the personal way out for intellectuals, and does not see the tens of thousands of labor reserves squeezed out of the countryside (naturally, there are also many intellectuals in this). (4) Speaking of individual intellectuals, "to find a rural area with abundant production and a secure livelihood... to live in this rural area..." Honestly, if there was a "relatively abundant production and a secure livelihood," they would not have rolled out of the "stable" countryside to this vast, unreliable city. Even if they came, and encountered setbacks, they would immediately go back, without having to consult the gentlemen of the "Readers' Advisory Column." You should know that now most rural children want to find wild vegetables, chop firewood, feed cattle..., helping their parents to do work to fill their stomachs. Schools do not cost money, but they are still unwilling to come. This is what I have seen with my own eyes. If "tens of thousands of returned students from various countries and graduates from universities and middle schools" still have some "relatively abundant and secure livelihoods..." that can accommodate them, they would have gone long ago and would not have to bother the "rural education theorists" to instruct them before they are willing to abandon the concept of "not loving the countryside" and stop staying in the unemployed and starving metropolis. To transform society, the entire society, aspiring young people should take the road of struggle. The individualistic, New Village-style reform movement is already outdated! (There are four more letters, to be published tomorrow)

Page 15

Free Talk

### Killing the Wrong Person 172

— Cao Juren

The other day, a newspaper carried a statement by a gentleman recounting the conversations of returnees from Changchun, saying: The Japanese have already completed the two major policies of "monopolizing opium" and "unifying the currency system" in the puppet state. These two things, which everyone thought were impossible to sort out in the old Zhang and young Zhang era, are now being handled in an orderly manner with a single wave of their hands. Therefore, the gentleman sighed: "I once discussed the harm of currency disorder with people from the Northeast, and all attributed it to the difficulty of reversing the accumulated problems, using it as an excuse for being difficult to handle. Why can the Japanese accomplish this in an instant? 'It is that they do not do it, not that they cannot do it.' This is a major root of the nation's illness!"

How can it be only a "root of illness"! The demise of the Chinese race and the overthrow of the Republic of China also lie in this phthisis. When a society, a nation, reaches old age, everything is "difficult to reverse the accumulated problems," so "revolution" is necessary. Revolution is a process of social upheaval; in the process, some good people, some bad people, and some people who are neither good nor bad will always be killed. Killing some people is not without a price; it has an isolating effect on society, dividing the old society and the new society into two distinct segments, so that the evil forces will not infect the new organization. Therefore, revolutionary killings should have standards and should kill more people over middle age, more people who represent the old forces. The success of the French Revolution lay in the sweeping away of the old forces during the Reign of Terror.

However, every revolution in China always goes against the norm. Many young people have sacrificed themselves by participating in revolutionary movements; in the process of revolution, the old forces temporarily hide away, but they are not eliminated at all; after the success of the revolution, the old forces re-emerge and make young people their sacrificial victims again, killing a large number of them. Mr. Sun Yat-sen worked hard for more than ten years on revolutionary work. The Xinhai Revolution succeeded, but Yuan Shikai took power and killed party members every day, even children of fifteen or sixteen years old; such a revolution not only does not have an isolating effect, but simply acts as a bodyguard for the old forces; therefore, since the Republic of China, there has only been senility, no vigor, and there is no need to talk about reform in any undertaking. As soon as reform is mentioned, it is bound to be "difficult to reverse the accumulated problems, using it as an excuse for being difficult to handle." […], its evil forces have been injected all the way to the present.

I call this abnormal state "killing the wrong person." I often say to my friends: "There is no such thing as a bloodless revolution. But 'blood' must not be shed on the wrong person. Killing Puyi earlier, killing more Zheng Xiaoxu and the like, is the great fortune of the country. If young people under the age of twenty-five are killed indiscriminately, reversing the natural order and undermining the vitality of society, then one can obtain the 'immediate retribution' of 'national subjugation and racial extinction.'"

Evening 173

— Jiang Ailun

It was already time to light the lamps, and Fuxian knew that she was already feeling weary, and that inevitable life was about to begin again. She sat lazily in front of the dressing table and began to tidy up. The mirror reflected her haggard shadow like a withered flower, and she felt even more like an aging beauty. The life of selling smiles that she had been playing with for the past few years, when she recalled it, she could not tell whether it was bitter or sour.

Her younger sister, Lixian, had already dressed up enchantingly, and like a little bird, flew east and flew west, chattering to her sister about some trivial matters about the neighbors next door and across the street. Although Fuxian had always loved her sister and never found anything bad about her, she felt a little annoyed with her sister today.

The notes sent from restaurants and taverns flew in one after another. Fuxian finally could not resist the urging of the rickshaw puller, put her sister on her lap, and let the rickshaw puller run quickly.

In this way, from one restaurant to one tavern, and then from that tavern to another restaurant, according to the urging of the notes, she dealt with them one by one, and then the sisters sat in a chartered car and ran back as before.

On the way home, Fuxian encountered many sisters who were living the same life of selling smiles, sitting in cars equipped with bright electric lights. She felt that they all had an incredible pride in their youth. The stimulation they gave her was really too great, so the scenes in the restaurants and taverns just now were reflected on her meninges one after another.

Those distinguished guests now mostly ignore her, and show unusual courtesy only to her sister Lixian, so Lixian is often surrounded by the guests, while she sits coldly in a corner. She noticed that her sister had learned to use a wonderful and charming gaze to bewitch those men who were chasing her. Needless to say, Lixian had received considerable training. But why can't she do the same? Why doesn't she understand the secrets of "autumn waves flirting and charming smiles"? But what if she did? Would those distinguished guests still have a good impression of Fuxian, who is in her thirties? This is something she herself does not believe.

She looked at her sister sitting on her lap and felt that her sister was like a delicate flower just beginning to bloom, while she was like fallen petals in March, the end of spring. However, when she thought of her sister being the same age as herself, she felt a blur in her eyes.

When they arrived at the door of their house, her sister saw a bag of tears in her sister's eyes as she got out of the car.

"Sister! What's wrong? Are you feeling unwell?"

"Sister! It's nothing." She took her sister's tender hand and kissed it.

Younger Brother 174

— Qiu Peng

Silently placing the wreath on the grave, all I could hear was the wild grass around me rustling in the wind. Thinking that my poor younger brother was lying alone beneath this pile of yellow earth, I couldn't help but feel an endless stream of sad memories涌 rise in my heart:

Three years after I was born, my younger brother was born into our family. Because he was born stupid since he was a child, he always suffered losses in everything. At school, he was often beaten by teachers and bullied by older children. When he returned home, his father never treated him with a kind word. Living in a family whose sustenance was already very poor, my younger brother was even worse, often struggling in an environment of hunger and cold.

At the age of thirteen, after graduating from elementary school, his father sent him to work as an apprentice in a grocery store in a small town more than ten miles away from home. The store had only one boss, and my younger brother worshiped that person as his teacher. Later, every time I went to that store to see him, I always saw the boss sitting leisurely in the store peeling his nails, while my younger brother, with his head and face covered in coal dust, kept drilling out of the kitchen and then drilling back in. After finally catching a break and talking to him, he quietly told me with tears in his eyes:

"The teacher wants me to do things in the store and also wants me to cook. If I don't cook well, or accidentally break a bowl, he will beat me and scold me... I don't want to live here, brother, take me back!"

"If you go back, Dad will beat you to death. Be patient and stay here for a while!"

Although my heart was filled with unbearable pain at letting him suffer there, I did not have the courage to take him back when I thought of my father's violent temper and the increasingly difficult family situation. But not long after, my younger brother finally ran back alone. When my father widened his eyes and furiously whipped him, I couldn't help but kneel down in front of my father with tears in my eyes and beg him for mercy.

Later, it happened that a friend of my father's opened a rice store in 乂乂 County, and my younger brother was transferred to that rice store to work as an apprentice.

Because it was relatively far away from there, I rarely had the opportunity to visit him afterwards. But from the letters he sent back each time, I knew that he was still struggling in a difficult environment. He said that because he had to help them carry the heavy bags of rice every day, he often felt pain in his bones all over his body at night. He also said that he had recently wanted to steal some time to read books and asked me to find some easy-to-understand books and send them to him. He said that every time he saw those fellows carrying their schoolbags to school, he felt jealous and hated, and was indescribably sad.

Two years later, a friend of mine was willing to introduce him to work as a student in a bookstore in 乂乂 County, Fujian Province.

When I told him this news, we were worried that he would not be willing to go. […], so young, to leave home alone for more than a thousand miles! But the fact was contrary to our expectations, and he actually agreed happily. He said that he would no longer have to do hard labor there, and he could also see many new books. He said that the bookstore was the paradise he had always dreamed of...

But unexpectedly, only a short year after going there, my younger brother died of illness in a foreign land with no relatives. When I suddenly received that telegram, my heart was truly like it had sunk into a bottomless abyss.

Now it has been a year since my younger brother's remains were moved back to his hometown and buried. Every time I pass by my younger brother's grave, I feel endless loss and sadness. When I think of all the suffering my younger brother endured in his short life of more than ten years, I can't help but shed tears. Really, it seems that my younger brother was born only to experience the hardships of the world and had no other purpose! What a cruel fate!

Long Creative Work

The Crossroads of Era and Love 175

— Zhang Ziping

"Mr. Lin looks down on people too much. I also graduated from a girls' middle school. Although my English grades are a bit poor, my Chinese essays are always graded A in every exam. I can even read Guo Moruo's translation of The Sorrows of Young Werther. What's more, it's just a love letter written to you by a girl from a girls' middle school! Mr. Lin, don't look down on people too much! ·········"

Haiquan listened to her say a lot, initially thinking she was joking. But later, seeing that there was still no trace of a smile on her face, and she hugged the child and walked back to her room without a word.

"This is really unexpected! I didn't know her temper was like this! Failed! Failed! I shouldn't have carelessly said the wrong word"!

Haiquan thought, since she is such a petty woman, then it would be better to apologize to her. So he also followed her into the room. He thought, he was going to participate in the demonstration parade this afternoon. If he was unlucky and was caught and sentenced by the ruling class to more than a year in prison, then he didn't know when he would be able to see them again. […], perhaps he would never see them again! Thinking of this, he felt sad again. He also thought that although he didn't feel that Qiuying was a very respectable woman, her heart was always good to him. On this point alone, he should happily maintain the friendship between the two.

"She is the only female friend I can see before participating in the demonstration parade!"

He inexplicably felt a burst of unnecessary sadness. In this instant, he regarded Qiuying as the incarnation of Peizhu and Madam Hezi.

He forgot her shallow and repulsive personality and felt that her demeanor was also somewhat moving.

"Madam, I said something wrong just now, I'm sorry. ·········"

"························"

But Qiuying sniffed and then exposed her breasts to feed the child, without saying a word, her face slightly lowered. But it could be seen that there were some smiles floating on her face. He thought, she is just playing this trick. A special impulse urged him to lean towards her.

The child, who had become familiar with him in the past few days, saw Haiquan approaching his mother, and threw away his mother's breast, turning around to giggle foolishly at Haiquan. Haiquan took the opportunity to lower his head and get closer to tease the child. His face almost touched her chest.

"He's eating milk!"

She smiled and scolded her child, putting the rose-colored nipple back into the child's mouth.

"Madam, are you angry with me like this? ·········"

"Who's angry with you? I'm not anything to you!"

Qu Lu Musings 176

— Zizhan

(15) Sichuanese and Tea

I previously wrote an article on Sichuanese and Opium, suspecting that the Chinese people's planting and consumption of opium originated with the Sichuanese. After reading Japanese scholar Yano Jinichi's "Modern Chinese Politics and Culture," which discusses the origin of Chinese people drinking tea, his research is precise and insightful, which inspired my thinking. I also suspect that the Chinese people's drinking of tea also originated with the Sichuanese. The ancient character did not have "tea," but only "tu." The character "tu" first appeared in the Book of Songs, such as "Who says tu is bitter? Its sweetness is like shepherd's purse." It is interpreted as a bitter vegetable, not belonging to the tree category. In the Erya's interpretation of trees, "jia" is "bitter tu." Guo Pu of the Jin Dynasty commented that the "jia" tree is small and similar to the gardenia. It produces leaves in winter that can be boiled into soup. Early picking is called "tu," and late picking is called "ming" or "chuan." People in Shu call it "bitter tu." This so-called "tu" is probably what we now call "tea." The Erya was traditionally said to have been written by the Duke of Zhou, supplemented by Confucius, added by Zixia, and supplemented by Shusun Tong. The Siku Quanshu Summary proves that its writing was after Mao Heng. It is mostly a compilation of old texts by philologists, which were gradually added to. To put it specifically, the earliest mention of drinking tea is found in the Erya. The practice of drinking tea began no later than the early Han Dynasty. The people of Shu called it "bitter tu," which can be said to be particularly knowledgeable of the taste. During the reign of Emperor Xuan of Han, Wang Bao wrote the "Slave Contract," which contains the phrases "roasting turtle and boiling tu" and "buying tu in Wuyang." Zhang Qiao of the Song Dynasty commented that the former "tu" is a bitter vegetable, and the latter "tu" is tea. Wuyang is Wang Bao's hometown, which now belongs to Pengshan County, Sichuan. Buying tea must be done in Wuyang. Could Wuyang have already been a famous tea-producing area at that time? Sun Chu's poem in the early Jin Dynasty also mentioned that Shu was the earliest place to produce tea. Zhang Qiao's interpretation of the "tu" in "buying tu in Wuyang" as tea is certainly not unreasonable. Zhang Zai of the Jin Dynasty was in Chengdu and wrote a poem when he ascended the White Rabbit Tower, saying, "May I ask about Yang Xiong's residence? I can imagine Sima Xiangru's hut." He also said, "Fragrant tea crowns the six pure [drinks], its flavor spreads throughout the nine regions. If life can be peaceful and happy, then this land can be enjoyed." Lu Yu of the Tang Dynasty, in his "Classic of Tea," listed famous figures who loved tea throughout history, saying, "In the Han Dynasty, there were Yang Xiong and Sima Xiangru." Sima Xiangru's "Fan Jiang Pian" has the character "chuan," and Wei Zhao's biography in the "Records of Wu" has the phrase "tu chuan to substitute for wine." The "Classic of Tea" also quotes Yang Xiong's "Dialects," saying that the people of Shu and the southwest call tea "she." Based on the above statements, it can be seen that since the Han Dynasty, when the custom of drinking tea first appeared, the people of Sichuan have had a special connection with tea. Sichuan was a famous tea-producing area, and the masters of prose and poetry in Shu, such as Sima Xiangru, Wang Bao, and Yang Xiong, were all famous tea lovers of the time.

The first time was during the university's 25th anniversary. If we can unite and persevere, there is nothing in the world that we cannot achieve. As of last night, the number of Chinese and foreign visitors to the exhibition has reached 304,000. Children, servants, and those who entered without tickets are not included. We hope that the 40th anniversary will be even grander.

Mayor Wu's Address: I just heard Li Zhaohuan report that the number of participating manufacturers and visitors to this exhibition is very high. In recent years, when domestic and foreign troubles have been pressing down on us, there has been much destruction. However, the people's enthusiasm for supporting construction has not diminished, which is very gratifying. Every day we see various political and economic conflicts between countries in the newspapers, and China is not exempt from this. Tracing the root cause, it is mostly due to economic reasons. Such economic problems, in countries with developed industries, are due to overproduction and the excessive importance of capital utilization. Even in China, where various industries have not yet reached the stage of mechanization, we have already entered the whirlpool. The disease of other countries is overproduction, while China's problem is insufficient production. Therefore, if we want to solve the unrest in today's society, we must first solve the China problem. Solving the China problem will greatly benefit the solution of world problems. Our party's Sun Yat-sen advocated international cooperation to assist China, so that China can become the center of the world's economic problems and solve the world's disputes. Therefore, we must first build China and make China prosperous. Today, Jiaotong University has an industrial and railway exhibition. Although this exhibition is only a part, the spirit of international cooperation has a great impact on China's future.

He also raised his glass in congratulations. Next, Director of the Central Mint En and Zhu Maodeng also delivered similar speeches. The meeting adjourned at 11:00 PM.

Ye Gongchuo's Address: Former President Ye Gongchuo gave a sincere training speech at the 37th anniversary meeting the other day. It is appended as follows: Today our university is holding the 37th anniversary ceremony. I happen to be in Shanghai and am very honored to be invited to participate by President Li. I have a few opinions on our university and would like to take this opportunity to express them. This anniversary is of great significance in the history of our university. You must all be very pleased to see the achievements of our university today, and I have even deeper hopes for the future of our university. Especially, I feel the close relationship between our university and the future of our country and society, so I would like to say a few sincere words, not ordinary generalities. Especially, my relationship with the duties of our university, although intermittent, has never been interrupted in spirit. Therefore, what I want to say today is only concerned with whether it is beneficial to our university, and whether it is pleasing to the ear is not a consideration. Our university has already had such achievements in the past, and may bring about even greater responsibilities in the future. Why is this? Because looking around the country, there is currently a great need for specialized academic talents everywhere. Our university has demonstrated achievements in various fields in the past, so all fields regard our university as a school that supplies talents for future construction. However, how our university should bear such a major responsibility is truly worthy of study. Although our university has a long history of 37 years, its development has only been in the last ten years. If we carefully examine the current content of our university, whether it has reached perfection, I am afraid no one would dare to say so. Therefore, for the past achievements of our university, we should thank the efforts of all faculty, staff, and students. For the responsibilities of our university, I hope you will continue to bear them. For example, just looking at the school buildings, this star needs to be renovated early. In addition, the Ping and Tang courtyards urgently need renovation, and the content needs to be sorted out and supplemented. These are too numerous to mention. Every time I think of the magnitude of future responsibilities, I feel that the content of our university must be further enriched. However, this matter cannot be done by one person or a few people in a short time. I hope that all faculty, staff, and students will work together to achieve the final goal. This is one of my hopes for our university. Secondly, our university has made many contributions to society in the past. Just take the example of radio. Although this science is very popular now, and there are many radio technology talents, in the past there were no such talents in the country, or it was even thought that there was no need for such talents. However, our university disregarded everything and created many radio talents for the country for today's use. From this point alone, it can be seen that the talents cultivated by our university are indeed beneficial to the country and society. However, social conditions are changing with each passing day, and the methods of schools in various countries to cultivate talents to meet the needs of the country and society are also increasing, and often schools and various undertakings are integrated. The teaching of schools and the training of institutions are integrated, so money and time are very economical. In the past, after students graduated and left school, they served in various fields and progressed according to their own circumstances. There was no fixed plan for both supply and demand, and the purpose was to cultivate talents. Therefore, the result is still the disease of uneconomical use of talents. In the future, schools and society must have a closer relationship. Students must be prepared and trained in school to serve the country and society in the future, so that after graduation, they can serve the country and society and be competent and happy. There are many things that can be learned from other countries in this regard. I sincerely hope that our university can adopt effective methods in the future to connect schools and social undertakings. This is my second hope for our university. In addition, there is one more opinion, which is about the academic atmosphere. Students of our university have excellent academic achievements, and their employment prospects can also win good reviews in society. However, what I want to say today is active, not passive. Each famous university in Europe and the United States has a special academic atmosphere. Although the beauty of our university's academic atmosphere has a place among the universities in the country, it has not yet produced a special atmosphere that other schools do not have. Our university has merged the three courtyards of Shanghai, Ping, and Tang into one university for ten years. However, because the courtyards are scattered in various places and each has a special history, they have not been able to integrate into one university in spirit. I sincerely hope that in the future, through the improvement of academic and educational systems, the three courtyards can be integrated into a whole organization, and from this whole organization, a unique spirit of Jiaotong University as a whole can be generated. This is my third hope for our university. Finally, regarding the issue of enriching the content of our university, I mentioned the issue of the research institute. Our country has never had a well-run research institute. If general university graduates are interested in further study, they must go abroad. Therefore, if our university wants to create a truly profound academic institution, it should quickly prepare to establish a very complete research institute to prepare the people of the country to study profound knowledge. This is my fourth hope for our university. Due to the limited time, what I have said above is only a brief outline. The details are not exhaustive. I hope you will pay attention to drawing inferences from one instance.
